ANTNEX 8
Page 1
BANGIADESH
POPULATION PROJECT
Information, Education and Communication Program
General Strategy
1.        The annex examines in general terms (a) the formulation of the
pilot schemes designed to integrate family planning education and motivation
with the development program of different ministries and (b) the need for
general support to the family planning information and education program for
nationwide extension. The details are given in separate annexes by ministries.
The section on pilot schemes describes their composition, coverage, common
facilities, organizational structure, timing and phasing and the underlying
training program. (See Chart 9412 which describes the training program-ot trte
pilot schemes.) The section on program support describes the project's support
for mass media and use of facilities provided in the project. This section
also describes the primary and secondary schools' population education program.
A. Introduction
2.        It is often stated that the programs of population planning that
proceed apart from economic development or social change are unlikely
to achieve the desired objectives of reduction in population growth rates.
The knowledge of the precise role of various factors in economic develop-
ment and social change that influence fertility behavior is inadequate.
But the experience of demographic transition in the past in Europe as well
as in countries with more recent experience indicates that perhaps the pro-
cess of modernization by changing the status of women and creating an awareness
of conflict between modernization and large-size families results in changing
the social attitude in favor of smaller family size norms. It is commendable
that the GOB, recognizing the significance of this relationship, has assigned
definite roles in population planning programs to ministries responsible
for education, information and rural development. This provides a broad
multisectoral approach to the population program in its First Five-Year Plan.
The following summarizes the roles of various ministries as stated in the
Plan document:



ANNEX 8
Page 2
(a)  The Ministry of Health and Family Planning will be
responsible for continuous motivation and supply of
family planning materials and services through couple
registration by health and family welfare multi-purpose
field workers.  The family planning program would be
integrated with health services for face-to-face
motivation, delivery of services and follow-up.
(b) The Ministry of Local Government, Rural Development,
and Cooperatives will develop women cooperatives for
increasing their employment potential through functional
literacy programs. Such programs will include education
on various social aspects of life including population
problems.
(c) The Ministry of Education will introduce population
education into the curricula of educational institutions
at all levels and into the program of adult education.
(d)  The Ministry of Agriculture will incorporate family
planning and nutrition education in agriculture
extension programs.
(e) The Ministry of Information and Broadcasting will have
programs for dissemination of information regarding
population problems and family planning through all
mass media including radio, T.V., newspapers, posters,
pamphlets, etc.
(f) The Ministry of Labor and Social Welfare will be
responsible for population and family planning education
and motivation through relevant social work programs.
3.        Realizing these objectives the project includes specific schemes
for all the above ministries to integrate population planning education and
motivation program (including contraceptive distribution in some cases) into
the development programs of different ministries. These programs are those
that will seemingly have greatest appeal to the population and have an
important direct relationship with population problems, e.g., women's literacy
and training, agricultural development and the school system. These schemes
are to be undertaken in a phased manner in order to learn as the schemes
proceed. The first phase forming part of the project is called the pilot
phase and the schemes are called pilot schemes.
B. Pilot Schemes
Broad Composition
4.        Following is the listing of pilot schemes in different ministries;
the details are given in a separate annex for each ministry:



ANNEX 8
Page 3
(a) Ministry of Local Government, and Rural Development, and
Cooperatives
(i)  Use of model farmers and cooperative managers
as change agents for family planning; and
(ii)  Rural women's functional literacy program as
a means of acceptance of family planning.
(b) Ministry of Labor and Social Welfare
(i) Rural mothers' clubs for family planning
motivation;
(ii) Women's vocational training program as a means
for acceptance of family planning; and
(iii) Population program for organized labor.
(c) Ministry of Agriculture
(i) Use of agricultural assistants for population
education.
(d) Ministry of Education
(i) Mobile population education team for seminars
on population education for school teachers.
(e) Ministry of Information and Broadcasting
(i) Use of audiovisual vans for family planning
films.
(f) Ministry of Health and Population Planning
(i) Family planning motivation kit for female
family welfare workers.
5.        Coverage:  The main criterion for determining the number as well
as the location of pilot thanas is that all the geographical areas with
different cultural, social, economic and administrative designs should be
covered by the schemes to delineate the impact of these factors on the fertility
behavior as well as on the success of the scheme. A minimum of one thana
from each of the 19 districts has been selected. Four pilot thanas - one
in each region - have been selected for the combined operation of seven out
of 9 pilot schemes to test the effect of coordinated and concentrated inputs
on fertility behavior. These would also help in developing the mechanism



ANNEX 8
Page  4
for coordination of interministerial schemes. These six out of nine schemes
are also to be operated in combination of two in thanas other than concentrated
thanas to allow the evaluation of their individual impact. The combination
consists of two schemes serving separate concentrated thana populations
(male and female) in the same thanas. The rest of the three schemes are to
be operated individually in special areas. The following is the distribution
of pilot schemes by the number of thanas (the list of thanas is given in
Table 1 and shown on the map at the end).

6.        Facilities:  The project includes funds, operating costs, vehicles
and equipment for the pilot schemes (see Annexes 9-14). Each ministry
will appoint an officer responsible for the pilot schemes. These officers
will receive three months training/orientation abroad to observe work done
in relevant institutions and in similar programs in other countries.
7.        Organization:  Each ministry will be responsible for the implemen-
tation of the respective pilot schemes through its population program officers
(PPO). The Population Planning Division (PPD) will be responsible for the
coordination of activities of various ministries through the support of the
coordination committees which have been proposed to be formed at national
district and thana levels in the First Five-Year Plan.
8.        Planning of Activities:  Resource persons identified in various
ministries have prepared the population programs in their respective ministries.
The details of each scheme will be worked out by the PPOs in collaboration with
the advisers that are provided for most of the schemes. It is further recom-
mended that an information, education and communication (IEC) working group
be created under the Health and Population Planning Section of the Planning
Comnission (PPS) to assist the Section in technical evaluation of the scheme
and in providing new ideas.



ANNEX 8
Page 6
9.        Evaluation:  The evaluation of the different schemes will be con-
ducted internally by the implementing ministries for which resources are
provided in the project. In addition, external evaluation will be con-
ducted by the PPS through its own proposed Evaluation Unit or through various
universities and research institutes. The project provides funds for such
evaluation studies and establishes the Evaluation Unit.
10.       Phasing and Timing:  It is proposed to start the pilot scheme by
the appointment of a population program officer preferably by early 1975 in
various ministries and arrange for their training abroad for three months.
The actual operation of the pilot scheme, is expected to start in August
1975 in half the thanas (28, including 4 concentrated thanas). The total
implementation period for these thanas would be three years. The other half
of the thanas would be taken up in the second year. Thus all the thanas will
have full operation for at least two years. At the end of each year's operation
the schemes will be evaluated for modification before continuing.
11.       Training:  The PPO will be responsible for arranging the training
of thana staff and the persons at the village level who would be involved
in the implementation of the scheme. The training will include education in
family planning and will cover the following aspects of the program:
(a) Knowledge of contraceptives, methods of birth control;
and lessons on conception and the biological process of
birth;
(b) Basic ideas on community development and population
problems;
(c) Motivation education approaches and techniques; and
(d) Use of publicity materials and communication aids
for family planning.
The chart at the end summarizes the organization of the training program.
C. General Program Support
Mass Media
12.       In addition to the above pilot schemes the project includes general
program support for (a) strengthening the mass media activities and (b)
introduction of population education in the school curriculum. It is said
that, in most circumstances, the face-to-face approach is the most effective
manner in which to motivate people towards the adoption of family planning
practice. But, given a population of 75 million and a shortage of staff



A1N,X 8
Page 7
and resources, it would be difficult to adopt face-to-face methods on a
nation-wide basis. Therefore, the project will rely heavily on the part
played by the Ministry of Information and Broadcasting and its use of the
mass media. People usually become aware of new ideas through public informa-
tion programs or from other people who have heard those programs. They are
then influenced by other sources of information/motivation before accepting
the new ideas and acting on them. The media, particularly the film, will
therefore endeavor to play a motivational role by using a strong emotional
appeal. This appeal will be backed by productions of a more direct informa-
tional approach as well as by the supporting work of the staff of the project
in the field. The project will use different types of media and evaluate
themn in different areas. Radio, films, film slides and tape recordings will
all play a part and, as the project progresses, it will be possible to assess
the value of each method with a view to an eventual increase in its use.
The project therefore strengthens the mass media work of the Ministry of
Information and Broadcasting by: (a) establishing a Population Cell in Radio
Bangladesh, (b) expanding the production capacity of the Films Department for
production of family planning films, (c) setting up a Population Feature
Writers Bureau and (d) training a public relations officer in family planning.
The use of media facilities is shown in Chart 9411 at the end of this annex.
Curriculum Development
13.       To prepare the younger generation better, it is essential to
introduce population education in the school curriculum. About 73% of the
primary school age-group children (6-10 years) and about 25% of children
in secondary schools, ages 11-15 years, are expected to be enrolled by
1977-78. The project includes support for curriculum development and
teachers' training.

BANGLADESH
POPULATION PROJECT
Population Program of the Ministry of Local Government,
Rural Development, and Cooperatives
1.        This annex (a) examines the ongoing program at the Ministry of
Local Government, Rural Development, and Cooperatives (MLGRDC) within which
the population program can be incorporated, (b) suggests an organization
for the implementation of population programs within MLGRDC and (c) outlines
specific schemes for the population program that the project would support:
their content, coverage, administration, evaluation, facilities and work
schedule.
I. Ongoing Programs
2.        The development program of the MLGRDC which is called the integrated
rural development program (IRDP) is designed to promote, develop and support
local institutions with local leadership to involve them in the implement-
ation of official development policies and measures. This type of program
has had tremendous success in the experiments conducted by the Bangladesh
Academy of Rural Development (BARD) at Comilla. The IRDP program is based
on the use of two-tier cooperative systems in rural areas for various develop-
ment programs.  It envisages that apart from serving as an effective tool
for increased agricultural production, the storage and marketing facilities
of cooperatives could serve as a base for bringing desired changes in the
field of health, family planning, functional education, and in the total
process of rural development.
3.        The first tier of the two-tier cooperative system consists of
village level cooperative societies called primary cooperatives having on
an average 40-50 members. These primary societies - one in each village -
are federated into the Thana Central Cooperative Association (TCCA). The
latter supervises the activities of the primary societies, provides easy
credit and arranges the training of selected members of the cooperative like
the manager and a model farmer at the Thana Training and Development Center
(TTDC). The TCCA's operations are conducted by elected managing committees.
A project officer and a deputy project officer appointed by the Ministry in
each thana serve as manager and paid secretary of this committee. At the
district level a project director supervises and coordinates the activities
of the TCCA.



ANNEX 9
Page 2
4.        At present, in 83 thanas with well-established IRDP programs, enter-
prising farmers (one from each society) and elected managers of the coopera-
tive societies at the village level are brought to the TTDC every week for
training. The IRDP is likely to cover half the thanas in the country by the
end of the First Five-Year Plan period. The IRDP also proposes to form
cooperatives for women and make it a base for social development programs.
The project providesadditional resources to introduce family planning in the
training of model farmers and cooperative managers so that they can be used
as change agents. Also the project totally supports the development of
functional literacy programs for rural women that would include training in
family planning through the women's cooperatives.
II. Organization for the Population Program at the Ministry
of Local Government, Rural Development and Cooperatives
A population program officer (PPO) responsible for the population
program and an assistant will be appointed as a part of IRDP in the Ministry.
The PPO will be of the level of Deputy Director and will report directly to
the Director-General, IRDP (Terms of Reference given in Appendix I). The
PPO will receive three months training at institutions abroad doing research
on communications for family planning motivation and rural development. They
will also visit countries with experience in such programs. An adviser for
twelve man-months would also be provided to assist the PPO in designing and
evaluating the scheme in addition to the training of personnel (Terms of
Reference are given in Appendix I).
6.        At the thana level one deputy project officer and one assistant
inspector-cum-trainer (mdinly for the model farmers' program) and two inspector-
cum-trainers (mainly for the women's program) in each of the nineteen pilot
thanas would be responsible for training and field supervision. They would
report in the field to the existing IRDP project officers at the thana and
district levels who would be responsible for the implementation of both
schemes in the field (see organization chart 9406 at the end of this annex).
7.        The internal evaluation of the scheme would be the responsibility
of the existing evaluation unit at TRDP that has adequate sanctioned positions.
The IPDP has created 31 professional positions for statistics, research
and evaluation, including fleld staff for its ongoing programs, of which
onlv two positions of Deputy Director and Assistant Director for Statistics
have been filled. On the assumption that the other senior positions will
also be filled soon, and the services of these officials would be available
for the internal evaluation of both pilot schemes, only two additional posts
of statistical assistants are provided in the project for internal evaluation
of the scheme.



ANNEX 9
Page 3
III. Rural Women's Functional Literacy Programs
8.        Objective:  To open opportunities (a) for instilling among rural
women an appreciation of the need for home development and child care, (b) for
motivating them to accept small family-size norms to help ensure a more
satisfactory future for their families and (c) for creating a sense of
independence by opening the possibility of earning a living through various
training programs that will hopefully be conducive to lowering the fertility.
9.        Content:  The scheme is designed to enroll rural women as members
of producers' cooperatives and to organize a functional literacy program for
those who would join the cooperatives by making a small deposit. The
functional literacy program would consist of adult literacy classes, educa-
tion and motivation in family planning, child care, nutrition, home develop-
ment and sanitation along with training in various functions like sewing,
poultry raising, kitchen gardening, etc. The training would be in selected
villages of the thana for about six months in two trades according to the
suitability to the members. Out of six month's training about three months
will be devoted to family planning, nutrition, home development, etc. The
program at the village level will be organized by five organizers selected
from each village according to their capability. These organizers will
receive honoraria and will be trained in the above described functions at
the thana level. These village organizers would also be given supplies of
contraceptives for distribution. During the period of training the members
will be charged the small amount of Tk. 2 per month as a token of their
interest. It would also cover part of the recurring cost. After the members
have learned the necessary skills the cooperatives would arrange credit to
enable them to get the necessary additional equipment and raw material according
to their trade preference. The cooperatives would also arrange for marketing
the products produced by the members during and after their training.
10.       Coverage:  The scheme will cover nineteen thanas - one in each
district. Within each thana ten villages would be selected for the women's
program. Thus about 190 villages in all would be covered by the scheme. The
scheme will operate in a phased manner - ten thanas (four concentrated thanas
and six others) will start the scheme in the first year and the rest of the
nine thanas in the second year.
11.       Expected Results:  Five village organizers from each village or
a total of 950 organizers (19 thanas X 10 villages X 5 organizers) will
receive intensive training at the thana level. If these village organizers
succeed in training 20 cooperative members (4 members per organizer) every
six months from each village the number of women exposed to such program
would be about 40 per village annually or 400 per thana or a total of
4,000 women (10 thanas X 10 villages X 20 members X 2 times a year) in the
first year; 7,600 women (19 thanas X 10 villages X 20 members X 2 times a
year) each in the second and the third years. In all, over 20,000 women



ANNEX 9
Page 4
including women organizers will be trained during the life of the scheme.
However, the indirect impact of awakening other women of the villages
to the possibilities of improving their status and increasing their earnings
are expected to be substantial. If only one-fourth of the women covered
are motivated for family planning about 4,000 to 5,000 acceptors would
result directly from the scheme during the three years.
12.       Administration:  The PPO will be responsible for preparing the
detailed plan for the implementation of the scheme and arranging for training
of staff and production of training material with the assistance of advisers.
The existing district and thana IRDP staff and the new staff will be
responsible for the execution of the scheme and they will receive orientation
in Dacca for about two to three weeks. A six-month training will be given
to the village organizer in various trades at the thana and another three
months on the job in the village. The trainers will be full-time inspectors-
cum-trainers recruited for the scheme. Out of three months training half the
time would be devoted to train them in holding adult literacy classes and in
family planning, nutrition, home development and education. In family planning,
training assistance would be obtained from MOHPP staff at the thana level.
The assistant inspector, under the guidance of the existing IRDP project
director and deputy project officer at the thana level, would be responsible
for the training program and would obtain audiovisual material from the head-
quarters.
13.       The operation of the scheme will be supervised at the village level
by the inspectors cum trainers. After giving three months' training to the
women organizers the two inspector trainers would spend an average of eight
weeks in each village supervising and technically assisting the implementation
of the program. The PPO, assistant PPO and inspectors will make frequent
spot field checks.
14.       Internal Evaluation:  While the external evaluation of the schemes
will be conducted by the PPS at the Planning Commission the internal evalua-
tion within the Ministry would consist of regular reporting, periodic evalua-
tion and special evaluation studies that will be conducted in collaboration
with the PPD at the MOHPP.
(a) Regular Reporting: The inspector will be responsible
for monthly reports that will provide information on:
(i) the number of village organizers trained and
functioning in each of the 10 villages selected for
the scheme in the thana; (ii) the number of female
cooperative members in the villages; (iii) the number
undergoing training; (iv) the number completed training;
(v) the dropouts from the schemes and reasons for dropping
out; (vi) brief notes on marketing facilities for items
produced by the members and their financial accounts;



ANNEX 9
Page 5
and (vii) characteristics of members using contraceptives.
Copies of the report will be sent through the district
office to the headquarters in Dacca, and to the PPD.
(b) Periodic Evaluation: The following assessment will be
made through periodic evaluation:
(i) Effectiveness of training of village organizers by
measuring their knowledge of implementation of
adult literacy scheme, knowledge of family planning,
and levels of knowledge and skills relating to the
trades and general education.  This can be done
through the application of simple tests before and
after the training.
(ii) Effectiveness of training given by village organizers
to cooperative members by measuring levels of
literacy and skills, and knowledge of family planning,
before and after training.  The inspectors should also
observe the members performing the functions and report
the levels of their skills after the training. They
should also prepare a brief report on the credit
facilities made available to the members for the purchase
of equipment, and on the maintenance of the equipment.
(iii) Percentage of the number and categories of persons
trained and functioning compared to the targets.
(c) Special Studies: Funds would be provided to the MLGRDC by the
PPD for the following special studies:
(i) Half-yearly study of the increase in contraceptive
practice among the participants in the scheme
and in the villages and thanas under this scheme
in comparison to that in other villages in the
same thanas and among different thanas.
(ii) Half-yearly study of a comparative analysis of
performance of total schemes in different thanas
and causes of differentials.
(iii) Other studies as decided by the Director of IRDP
or by the PPO.
15.       Cost:  The total. cost of the scheme is estimated at USA371,6fl.
The dlctails are gpven in the table at the end of this annex.



ANNEX 9
Page 6
IV. Use of Model Farmers and Cooperative Managers
16.       Objective:  To create an understanding of population problems and
a sense of commitment for the population planning program among village
leaders to use them as agents of change. The model farmers and cooperative
managers are usually the enterprising and well-respected village members.
Their approach and ideas would be easily acceptable. Also in a male-dominated
society like Bangladesh the change in opinion and attitude of men is
essential for the success of the program.
17.       Content:  The model farmers and cooperative managers will be given
talks on the need for population planning, ways and means of family limita-
tion, and communication techniques at the weekly sessions at TTDC for about
three months. They in turn will arrange group sessions of cooperative
members to discuss the problems. The model farmers and cooperative managers
will be given a small amount (Tk. 5) per meeting on the basis of reports
submitted by them. At the end of the year the best model farmer in the thana,
judged by the sale of contraceptives and by other studies, would be given
the price of an agricultural implement costing about Tk. 2,500. The coopera-
tive managers will also be provided with a radio set to attract the people
to the meetings and provide an audience for the radio programs on the subject
prepared by a special cell to be established at Radio Bangladesh. The
maintenance of the radio would be charged to the profits of the cooperatives
to ensure proper use of the radio. The cooperative manager will have supplies
of contraceptives for distribution.
18.       Coverage:  The program will cover all the villages in 19 thanas -
one in each district. These thanas would be the same as those selected
for the women's functional literacy program. Ten thanas (four concentrated
thanas and six others) will be initiated in the scheme in the first year
and in the rest of the nine thanas in the second year.
19.       Expected Results:  About 3,800 model farmers and cooperative
managers from 1,900 villages (100 villages per thana X 19) will receive
training and orientation in population problems. If a model farmer and
cooperative manager jointly cover 7 persons of reproductive ages a week in
their weekly meetings and through radio programs, about 638,000 are expected
to be covered per year under this scheme when the 1,900 villages are in
full operation, in addition to 33,600 in the first year when only 1,000 vil-
lages would be covered. If 10% of these accept family planning, the number
of new acceptors would be about 54,000 per year or 2.8 per month per village.
20.       Administration:  The PPO will be responsible for preparing the
detailed plan for the implementation of the scheme and arrange for training
of staff and production of training material with the assistance of advisers.
The existing IRDP district and thana staff and the new staff recruited for



ANEX 9
Page 7
the scheme would first be given orientation and training at Dacca. They would
also visit the Comilla Academy of Rural Development for orientation. After
finishing the training they would help in drawing up the courses for three
months or about 90 hours for training of model farmers and cooperative managers
in population problems and programs. In actual training of model farmers
and cooperative managers the thana staff would obtain technical support from
the staff of the Ministry of Health and Population Planning. The training
material and audiovisual aid would be supplied by the headquarters. The
deputy thana PPO and the assistant inspector would be largely responsible
for supervisory field visits. They are expected to visit every village every
three months.
21.       Internal Evaluation:  While the external evaluation of the schemes
will be conducted by the PPS at the Planning Commission (See Annexes 18 and
19) the internal evaluation within the Ministry would consist of regular
reporting, periodic evaluation and special evaluation studies in collabora-
tion with the PPD at the MOHPP.
(a) Regular Reporting: The cooperative managers will
prepare simple monthly reports at the village level
which are handed over to the assistant inspector
when they visit thanas for weekly meetings. The
defaulters will be contacted by the assistant
inspector to obtain the reports due. The cooperative
managers will maintain a simple stock and an issue
registry for contraceptives. They would report monthly
on (a) contraceptives sold, (b) number of persons to
whom sold, (c) number of group meetings held, jointly
with model farmers, for cooperative members, (d) the
number attended, (e) the number of audience at the
radio program, and (f) impressions of the audience'
of family planning programs. At the thana level, a
monthly report will be prepared, incorporating the
above information for each village and giving the
number of cooperative managers and model farmers trained,
and the number still active. Copies of the report will
be sent through the district office to the headquarters,
and to the PPD. The health inspector will also give a
brief report on the use of radios.
(b) Periodic Evaluation: The following assessment will
be made through periodic evaluation:
(i) Effectiveness of training: The deputy thana PPO
and the assistant inspector will observe group
discussions organized by the cooperative managers
and farmers and send reports to headquarters
on the adequacy of knowledge of the managers and
model farmers in tackling questions raised in the
groups and on problems of keeping their interest alive.



ANNEX 9
Page 8
(c) Special Studies: Funds would be provided to the MLGRDC
by the PPD for the following special studies:
(i) Number of the two categories of persons trained
in the scheme and still active compared to the
targets.
(ii) Half-yearly comparison of family planning
acceptors within the scheme, with the cor-
responding numbers in thanas without the scheme.
(Copies of monthly reports for different thanas
on acceptors can be obtained from thana health
center or the MOHPP.)
22.       Cost:  The total cost of the scheme is estimated at US$956,460 for
about three years. The details are given in the table at the end of this annex.
V. Staff and Other Requirements for Both Schemes
23.       Personnel:
(a) One population program officer (PPO) with supporting
office staff (typist, peon) at the headquarters to
be responsible for detailed designing, implementation
and supervision of both the pilot schemes. Study
tour abroad for the PPO.
(b) An adviser for 12 man-months to assist the PPD.
(c) One assistant population program officer specifically
responsible for the women's program- for training
of field staff, production of material and marketing
of products.
(d) One deputy thana PPO in each thana to assist the
existing thana project officer in implementation
of the schemes.
(e) Two inspector-cum-trainers in each pilot thana
mainly for training the women's organizers and field
supervision.
(f) One assistant inspector-cum-trainer mainly for
training of model farmers and cooperative managers
and field supervision.



ANNEX 9
Page 9
(g) Two statistical assistants for the Evaluation Unit

BANGLADESH
POPULATION PROJECT
Terms of References
Population Program Officer
1.        The population program officer (PPO) will be responsible for finding
ways to integrate population planning programs in the Ministry's ongoing
activities and for the implementation of the pilot schemes particularly
for:
(a) Keeping a liaison with the PPD and PPS;
(b) Submitting quarterly reports to the PPD;
(c) Arranging for the training/orientation program of
the staff of the scheme;
(d) Arranging for internal evaluation of the scheme
analysis of routine data and feedback of the
results of evaluation to the staff of the scheme
and to the Director-General of IRDP;
(e) Receiving the results of evaluation from and
providing proper feedback to the staff of the
scheme;
(f) Making suitable modification in the scheme in the
light of evaluation results;
(g) Ensuring effective supervision of the scheme and
making frequent field visits (the PPO should be
in the field for at least three-fourths of the
time); and
(h) Ensuring the marketing of the products and proper
allocation of sale of proceeds to the cooperatives
and its members.



ANNEX 9
Appendix I
Page 2
Qualifications
2.        Preferably a senior civil servant from the ministry concerned.
Adviser
(a) To assist the population planning officer in:
(1) detailed preparation of the pilot scheme
for the model farmers and cooperative managers
and women's functional literacy programs;
(ii) training and orientation of field personnel;
(iii) making improvements in the operation of the two
schemes;
(iv) establishment of a system of internal
evaluation;
(v)  setting up indices for external and internal
evaluations;
(vi) reviewing the schemes before the end of assignment
and making recommendations for further improvement.
Qualifications
3.        An expert of established reputation in the field of rural
development with specialization in communication techniques in population
programs.



ANNEX 1 0
Page 1
BANGLADESH
POPULATION PROJECT
Population Program of the Ministry of Labor and Social Welfare
1.        This annex examines (a) the ongoing programs of the Ministry of
Labor and Social Welfare within which the population program would be
incorporated and (b) the specific schemes designed for incorporating the
population program in the relevant activities - their organization, content,
coverage, administration, evaluation, facilities and work schedule.
I. Ongoing Program
2.        The Ministry of Labor and Social Welfare (MLSW) is preparing plans
for rural social service (RSS) schemes through its Directorate of Social
Welfare. The basic idea in social service schemes of the Ministry is to
encourage formation of voluntary groups for the provision of social services
and to support these groups through locally-recruited government social
welfare workers. At the headquarters the RSS will be headed by a Deputy
Director of Social Welfare who will have two Assistant Directors. At the
thana level the RSS will be headed by a social welfare officer. The social
welfare officer will have eight male and eight female village social workers
(two for each union). The main emphasis of the social service program is on
landless laborers or those with uneconomic holdings. About 20% of the rural
population is landless and another 42% of families have land of less than
one acre.
3.        The Directorate of Labor under the Ministry of Labor and Social
Welfare has about eighteen labor welfare centers in industrial areas.
Each labor welfare center has provision for medical services, adult educa-
tion, recreational facilities and counselling of workers and their families.
A national family planning seminar organized in November 1972 jointly by the
Government and WHO recognized industrial workers as a special target group
and recommended that the national family planning program should be strength-
ened through coordination with other development programs including 'labor
organizations in industry'. In implementation of this recommendation, a
National Committee for Population Planning in the labor sector was established
in February 1973 under the chairmanship of the Director of Labor. It has as
its members representatives of the trade unions, the employers' organizations
and the National Family Planning Board. Also courses in population were



ANNEX 10
Page   2
introduced at the Industrial Relations Institute at Tongi.  This Institute
provides an excellent opportunity to bring management, trade unions and
government officials together. This Committee in association with the
International Labor Organization (ILO) and with the financial assistance of
the United Nations Fund for Population Activities (UNFPA) conducted another
national labor/management seminar on population and family planning in the
organized sector in July 1973. The seminar strongly endorsed the need for
involving the labor ministry, employers and workers in the national family
planning program. The UNFPA is supporting (a) the introduction of a family
planning service in two labor welfare centers and, (b) strengthening of
population courses at the Industrial Relation Institute through technical
assistance and fellowships.
4.        The National Rehabilitation Board, a semi-autonomous body under
the MLSW, has been successful in providing vocational training and establishing
production centers for war victims. It now intends to expand its activities
to reach all women in rural areas. One of the program strategies adopted by
the Board is to render vocational training to the poor illiterate and semi-
literate women and subsequently rehabilitate them economically in their
respective environments with needed skills for earning their living. By now
the Board has organized 32 vocational training centers all over Bangladesh
and a total of nearly 6,000 women have been given such training. The Board
at present gives about eight weeks of training in family planning as part
of the program. A judge of the Supreme Court is the Chairman of the Board.
Other members include influential women leaders and professionals. The Board
has been able to cover a substantial portion of the recurring cost from the
sale proceeds of goods produced by the women workers.
5.        The project includes schemes to utilize the above described
structure for population programs through the:
a.   formation of mothers' clubs under the Directorate of Social
Welfare for family planning motivation as a part of rural
social services program;
b.   introduction of the population program for organized labor at
labor welfare centers and
c.   support of the vocational training of rural women through
the National Rehabilitation Board to cover a large number
of women for family planning motivation.
II. Rural Mothers' Clubs
6.        Objective:  To bring together currently married women who are
within the reproductive ages together (a) for gainful economic activity
through training in various trades and (b) for education in various aspects
of social life including population and family planning.



ANNEX 1 0
Page   3
7.        Organization:  At the headquarters a population program officer
(PPO) at the level of Deputy Director, specializing in home economics, would
be attached to the office of the Director, Social Welfare and would be mainly
resnonsible for the implementation of the program. (The terms of reference
are given in Appendix I.) The PPO will receive three months training/orienta-
tion abroad in countries where such programs have been succssful (e.g., Korea)
and in universities famous for research in communication. An adviser will
be provided to assist the PPO (the terms of reference are given in Appendix
I.) At the thana level existing social welfare officers will be responsible
for the implementation of the program with the help of female village social
workers. At the village level the elected officers of the Club would help
in the .rmplementation of the program. Training in various trades and educa-
tion including literacy, family planning and home development would be given
by specially appointed instructors (see organization chart 9407 at the end
of this annex).
8.        Contents:  Five villages from each of the eight unions in a thana
will be selected for the formation of mothers' clubs. The Government village
social worker would help in organizing the mothers' clubs. The clubs'
activities will include a literacy program, family planning education, home
economics (nutrition, fruit preservation, etc.), a recreational program and
vocational training in poultry raising, garment making, production of socks
and vests, carpet weaving, bamboo goods, etc. The education and training
will be rendered through specially-appointed instructors (2 instructors per
village) who would visit each village for three months. After six months of
training the club members will continue to use the clubs' equipment for the
production of goods. The equipment could be used by them during the time
of the day it is not used for training. The Ministry will make arrangements
for marketing the product when produced on a large scale. All profits will
be given to the producer except a small percentage of it that will be retained
by the village social worker (or elected secretary of the club) for replace-
ment of equipment. These clubs will also be used for the distribution of
conventional methods of contraception. The elected secretary of each club
will be responsible for such distribution and maintenance of records.
9.        Coverage:  One thana in each district (19) would be covered during
the three-year implementation period. In the first year only ten thanas
(four concentrated thanas and 6 others) will be selected. In the second year
another nine thanas will be included. The scheme will be modified in the
light of earlier experiences in the ten thanas. Five villages from each of
the eight unions in a thana will be selected for the formation of mothers'
clubs or 40 villages in each thana. Therefore, about 760 villages will be
covered by the scheme.
10.       Expected Results:  In all, 760 mothers' clubs - one in each village
or 40 per thana - will be formed. If, at a minimum, each club has ten
members, in the first year it is expected that 4,000 females from 400 clubs



ANNEX I 0
Page 4
will be educated and trained in each six-month period, thus totaling 8,000
for the year. In the second and third years with all 760 clubs in operation,
about 15,200 women would be trained annually. Thus about 38,400 women will
be covered by the program in the three years. If one-fourth of these women
accept family planning the number of new acceptors would be about 8,000 to
9,000 during the three years. Further, a change in attitudes of these women
towards family size will have an impact on others and set a multiplier effect.
11.       Administration:  The population program officer will be respon-
sible for working out the details of implementation of the program with
the help of the adviser. The existing social welfare officers will receive
orientation in the population program at Dacca for two to three weeks. Also
four-week training courses will be organized, by the PPO, for village social
workers in various aspects of population problems, communication techniques
and the organization of the scheme. The PPO will draw up the training courses
and invite guest lecturers from the Ministry of Health and Population Planning,
the Family Planning Association, the Research Institute, Comilla Academy, etc.
These courses will be introduced later as a part of the training program
at the Social Welfare In-service Training Center. The female and male
village social workers at the union level will assist in the formation of
clubs, election-of officers and will directly supervise the activities
of the clubs in five villages. Further, the social welfare officers from
thana level and PPOs from headquarters will make frequent visits for super-
vision of the scheme. Two trade instructors for each union will give
necessary training and hold literacy classes.
12.       Evaluations:  While the external evaluation of the schemes will be
conducted by the PPS at the Planning Commission the internal evaluation
within the Ministry would consist of regular reporting, periodic evaluation
and special evaluation studies in collaboration with the PPD at the MOHPP.
a.   Regular Reporting:  The trade instructors will prepare
monthly repworts for each village of the union in which they
work, giving information on: (i) number of mothers' clubs
formed, (ii) membership of the clubs, (iii) number of
members fully trained for various vocations and number of
dropouts and reasons for same, (iv) of the active members,
number following vocations in which they were trained, (v)
for the number not following, reasons; (vi) frequency of
meetings of clubs, (vii) brief review of functions of the
club, (viii) number of members who learned to read and write,
({x) number of contraceptives distributed. At the thana
level, the social welfare officer will add information on
the number of trade supervisors in position in each union.
Ile will also prepare a brief report on the maintenance
and use of the equipment given to clubs and marketing
facilities created for the items produced. Reports
will be relayed from union to thana to district and
to headquarters and the Inspection Directorate.



ANNEX 10
Page 5
b.   Periodic Evaluation:  The following assessments will be
made through the periodic evaluations:
(a) Effectiveness of the training given to social welfare
officers, trade inspectors and village social workers,
with the help of before- and after-training tests of
their knowledge and skills in the fields in which they
are trained;
(b) Percentage of the various.categories of persons specially
trained, and clubs formed as compared to targets;
(c) Of the persons trained, percentage of persons actively
participating, by social and economic classification of
persons, and by vocations followed; and
(d) Special Studies: Funds. would be provided to the MLSW by
the PPD for the following special studies:
{i) Increase in contraceptive practice of contraception
among the village social workers and members of
the clubs; in relation to the corresponding figures
for the other village, in the thana; and
(ii) The socio-economic effects of the clubs.

III. PoEulation Program for Organized Labor at Labor Welfare Centers
17.       Objectives:  To expand facilities in the three labor welfare centers
covering organized laborers and their families to: (a) provide family
planning services through its clinics and (b) or educate and motivate the
workers and their families for accepting the small family-size norm.
18.       Organization:  A Population Program Officer (PPO) at the level of a
Deputy Director will be responsible for implementation of the scheme. He will
be attached to the Office of the Director of Labor. (The terms of reference
for the PPO are given in Appendix I.) The PPO will be trained abroad for
three months in countries with population programs for organized labor and
in institutes dealing with family planning communications research. The
National Committee for Population Planning in the Ministry of Labor will act
as Advisory Committee for this scheme. The Committee would review the scheme
and assist in obtaining adequate cooperation and support from different
sections of labor organization. At the labor welfare center the medical
officer would be in charge of the program.  Advisory services for six man-
months are provided to assist in formation of plans and training of personnel.
19.       Contents:  The existing medical officer in the centers will deliver
family planning services and advise the workers and their families on
contraception while they visit the clinics. Two family planning visitors
will be assigned to assist the medical officer and to talk to the patients.
Also, six male and six female social welfare workers in each center would
be responsible for face-to-face motivation and for home visiting in and around
the area and in distant villages where workers' families reside. Influential
labor leaders will be requested to speak in various meetings on the popula-
tion problem.



ANNEX 1 0
Page 8
20.       Coverage:  One labor welfare center in each of the three industrial
areas, namely Chittagong, Khulna and Bogra would be covered. These centers
are for labor engaged in cement, glass and steel factories, the paper mill,
oil refinery and dock work at Chittagong, and in the shipyard, paper mill,
jute mill and newsprint work at Khulna and in ceramics and cotton factories
at Bogra.
21.       Expected Results:  The scheme is likely to cover a population
of 50,000 in these industrial belts, of which about 90% is stated to be in the
reproductive ages. If about 50% accept family planning practices, the number
of new acceptors would be over 20,000 during the three-year period. The
scheme, which provides for contacting the families as well, is expected to
have a wider effect in the rural areas where a large proportion of the workers'
families reside.
22.       Administration;  The population program officer, with the assist-
ance of the adviser, will be responsible for the detailed preparation of
the scheme. The training program for medical, paramedical staff and field
motivators in the delivery of family planning service techniques of communica-
tion and motivation, would be arranged by the PPO at Dacca for 2-3 weeks.
He would obtain assistance from the Industrial Relations Institute, the
Family Planning Association and the Ministry of Health and Population Planning.
The PPO will closely supervise the work of the motivators and follow-up the
work at the welfare center clinics. The clerk in each center will keep the
clinic records.
23.        Evaluations:          While the external evaluation of the schemes
will be conducted by the PPS at the Planning Commission the internal evaluation
within the Ministry would consist of regular reporting, periodic evaluation
and special evaluation studies in collaboration with the PPD at the MOHPP.
(a) Regular Reporting: The clinics will maintain some general
clinic records including client and acceptor characteristic
forms, and the form for the monthly reporton performance
as in the ongoing family planning program of the MOHPP in
urban areas. The paramedical persons at the clinics will
prepare the monthly reports, by area covered. Copies of
monthly reports, together with copies of the acceptors'
characteristic forms will be sent to the Directorate of
Labor and the PPD.
(b) Periodic Evaluation: The following assessment will be made
through periodic evaluation: (i) monthly rate of new
acceptors per 1,000 population or 100 eligible couples to be
covered (both estimated), in the month and cumulatively,
by method and area; (ii) monthly tabulations of couples
contacted by status of acceptance (new, old or non-acceptors)
in the month and cumulatively by area; (iii) number of old
acceptors continuing old method, changed methods, or



ANNEX 10
Page 9
discontinued contraception, by method and by area;
(iv) monthly tabulations of estimated couple years of
protection, by method and by area; (v) half-yearly
tabulations of new acceptors, by characteristics and by
area and (vi) annual review of the scheme, with the
clinic staff.
c.   Special Studies:  Funds would be provided to the MLSW by
the PPD for the following special studies:
(i) periodic assessment of use-effectiveness and
extended use-effectiveness of contraceptive
methods; and
(ii) follow-up of drop-outs.
Staff and Other Requirements
25.       Personnel:  Additional personnel in the project consists of:
(a) A PPO at headquarters to assist the Director of Labor
in implementing the scheme;
(b) one adviser to assist the PPO for six man-months;
(c) Six paramedical personnel - two in each center to assist
the medical officer;
(d) Three clerks - one in each center to keep records;
(e) Twelve motivators at each center for home visiting and
face-to-face motivation of workers and their families,
plus two field workers at each center;
(f) A stenographer for headquarters; and.
(g) Four drivers, and one messenger/peon.
26.       Vehicles and Equipment
(a) Four-wheel drive vehicles - one for headquarters' staff
for supervision and meetings with workers and one at each of
the three centers for home visiting.
(b) Three sets of audiovisual equipment is provided; it would
use films provided by the PPD and the Ministry of Information
and Broadcasting; and
(c) Two hand calculators for evaluation.

among the labor leaders, for the organization of meetings and internal
evaluation of the scheme.

29.       Cost:  The total cost of the scheme is estimated at US$239,000.
The details are given in the table at the end of this annex.
IV. Women's Vocational Training Program
30.       Objective:  The main objectives of the schemes are (a) to motivate
working women towards the acceptance of small family size norms, (b) to
observe the difference the employment of women can make on fertility behavior,
(c) to extend the population planning message through these working women to
the community and (d) to create a large number of community leaders among
women in the areas of population planning and economic activities.
31.       Organization:  The scheme will be part of the existing organiza-
tional structure. The National Rehabilitation Board (NRB) with its headquarters
in Dacca is responsible for the overall administration of the scheme. The
Chairman of the NRB functions as its executive head. At the district and



ANNEX 10 
Page 11
thana levels local conmittees are formed and they function under the guide-
lines of NRB. On behalf of the Chairman of the Local Committees, a field
organizer and full-time qualified officer appointed by the National Board
runs the program. She is assisted by two field assistants, trainers and
accountants, etc. At the headquarters the implementing units are of four
types (a) administration and finance, (b) vocational training, (c) marketing.
A Population Program Officer at the level of Deputy Director will be
specifically appointed for the implementation of the scheme at the headquarters
(terms of references are given at the end of this annex). He will report
to the Chairman, NRB. Other additional staff for the scheme, provided on the
existing pattern, will help in the implementation at the local level.
32.       Contents:  About nine months. of training (six months at the thana
and three months at the union) will be given to the women who join the
program. The training program will include courses in adult literacy, family
planning and two trades. The vocational training will vary from jute goods
preparation, doll making, secretarial work, garment-making and knitting, etc.
Training will also be given in light agricultural work and poultry raising.
The selection of trades in each center will depend upon availability of raw
materials, prospects of local marketing of the produced goods from a given
trade, practice of the trade in the area and also availability of skilled
hands in the given trades to be utilized as resource persons in the center.
Two takas per day will be given to the trainers and trainees at the thana
level and Tk 1.50 at union level centers.
33.       Coverage:  In all, eight thanas will be covered in phases - schemes
will start in four thanas in the first year and another four thanas in the
second year. About 32 unions and 128 villages will be covered under the
scheme.
34.      EExpected Results:  In each of the eight thanas 20 trainers will
instruct 20 newly recruited women for 9 months, with one trainer responsible
to each trainee. The trainer will perform her production assignment and
train and educate the trainee assigned to her. At the union level centers
15 trainers trained from the corresponding thanas (assuming five dropouts)
will function as production workers and will train 15 rural women every three
months. The trainers turned out from the union centers will go back to their
villages and act as production workers and population educators. It is
expected that about 160 women (20 trainees X 4 thanas X 2 times a year) would
be trained in the first year and 320 each in the second and third years each
at the tlhana level. Similarly, at the union level in the first year 480
women (15 trainees X 16 unions X 2 times in the first year) will be trained,
followed by 960 (15 trainers X 16 unions X 4 times a year) in the second and
third years each. Thus, during the three-year project period about 800 will
be trained at the thana level and 2,400 at the union level or over 3,200
in all. If 10 of these 15 women trained at the union level organize the
production center in their villages and succeed in training 10 women the
number of women covered would be about 3,200 in the first year, 12,800 in the
second and third years, or 16,000 in 3 years. If about 25% of the women
covered including the union organizers accept family planning, the total
number of new acceptors may be over 2,500.



ANNEX 10
Page  12
35.       Administration:  The Population Program Officer will specifically
be responsible for the detailed preparation of the scheme. At the thana
level a field organizer and two field assistants will be responsible for
organizing the training program.  The staff of the scheme would be trained
by the present staff engaged in such work in addition to the Family Planning
Association and the Ministry of Health and Population Planning staff. The
training in family planning for eight to twelve weeks will be given by the
field staff and guest lecturers.
36.       Evaluations:  While the external evaluation of the schemes will be
conducted by the PPS at the Planning Commission, the internal evaluation
within the Ministry would consist of regular reporting, periodic evaluation
and special evaluation studies in collaboration with the PPD at the MDHPP.
(a)  Regular Reporting:  The field officers will be responsible
for monthly reports that will provide information on: (i)
numbers trained, (ii) attendance at family planning sessions,
(iii) number of contraceptives distributed and (iv) the
output of products every quarter. The report will be sent
by the chairman of the local committee to the headquarters
and the PPD.
(b) Periodic Evaluation: The following assessment will be made
through periodic evaluation: (i) effectiveness of the train-
ing given to the workers, with the help of before-and after-
training tests of their knowledge and skills in the fields
in which they are trained, (ii) percentage of the various
categories of persons specially trained as compared to targets,
(iii) of the persons trained, percentage of persons actively
participating, by social and economic classification of persons,
and by vocations followed.
(c) Special Studies: Funds would be provided to the women's
vocational training program by the PPS for the following
special studies: (i) on the increase in practice of contra-
ception among the participants in relation to the cor-
responding figures for the villages, unions and thanas
and (ii) a comparative analysis of performance of
different thanas and unions.
Staff and Other Requirements
37.       Personnel
(a) A population program officer and support staff at the headquarters;
(b) Fight field organizers, one per thana;

(d) Sixteen field supervisors and sixteen guest lecturers
(two for each thana and four for the union).

(a) Four portable tape recorders;
(b) Equipment for training in various trades and light
agricultural practices;
(c) Two 4-wheel drive vehicles for headquarters, eight
motorcycles for the thana and 32 bicycles for the
production centers; and
(d) Office equipment.

(a) Maintenance of vehicles; and
(b) Allowances for trainers and trainees.

The cost of the scheme is estimated at US$496,700. The details
are given in the table at the end of this annex.

Terms of References of the Population Program Officer at the Directorate of
Social Welfare
Population Program Officer
1.        The population program officer will be responsible for:
(a)  Keeping liaison with the PPD and the PPS;
(b) Submitting regular quarterly reports to the PPD;
(c) Arranging for the training/orientation program for the staff
of the scheme;
(d) Arranging for an internal evaluation of the scheme, including
analysis of routine data and feedback of the results of
evaluation to the staff of the scheme and the Director of
Social Welfare;
(e) Receiving the results of evaluation and providing proper
feedback to the staff of the scheme;
(f) Making suitable modification in the scheme based on
of evaluation results;
(g) Ensuring effective supervision of the scheme and making
frequent field visits (the PPO should be in the field
for at least three-fourths of the time); and
(h) Ensuring the marketing of products and proper allocation
of sale proceeds to the members of the club.
Qualifications
2.        Preferably a senior civil servant from the ministry concerned.

Adviser at the Directorate of Social Welfare
1.        The adviser will assist the Director of Social Welfare in:

in techniques of population education and motivation

(d) laying down the criteria for internal and external
evaluations;
(e)  establishing the system of internal evaluation; and
(f) review of the program before the end of the assignment
and then making recommendation for its improvements.
Qualifications
An expert of established reputation in the field of communications
with experience in administering or planning similar programs in less-
developed countries.

ANNEX 11
Page 1
BANGLADESIT
POPULATION PROJECT
Population Program of the 1linistry of Agriculture
1.        This annex briefly discusses the present function of the agricul-
tural assistants of the Ministry of Agriculture in which population education
can effectively be included, the organization required for the purpose (see
organizational chart 9408), the objective and contents of this scheme, facilities
provided by the project, and the work schedule.
T.  Ongoing Program
2.        Among all the services of the Government of Bangladesh, only the
agricultural extension service has agents in all unions. Its main function
is to provide educational services to the farmers pertaining to the agri-
cultural development. These services are rendered through more than 4,noo
agricultural assistants - one in each union.  These agricultural assistants,
with established positions of leadership and extensive involvement in formal
and informal group activities in the rural areas, have gained much experience
in formal education. The Ministry also has agricultural officers at both
district and thana levels for supervising the work of these assistants.
The project includes a pilot scheme for the use of these agricultural
assistants in population and family planning education.
II. Use of Agricultural Assistants
3.        Objective:  To help farmers understand (a) the population problem
in terms of the adverse effect of population growth on the availability of
resources, production of output and levels of living and (b) possible ways
and means of solving the population problem.
4.        Organization:  A population program officer (PPO) at the level of
Deputy Director in the Ministry of Agricultture will be appointed who will
report to the Director of Agriculture. He would be mainly responsible for
the implementation of the pilot scheme. Ile will- also suggest ways of includ-
ing population education in the other programs of the ministries particularly
the introduction of population education into the regular curriculum of



ANNEX 1 1
Page   2
Agricultural Assistants Training Institutes in the country. Additional
equipment for production of slides on population problems is being provided
for the Agricultural Information Services. These slides will be used by agri-
cultural assistants as well as by other ministries. The PPO will ensure the
production and time availability of slides to all concerned ministries (terms
of reference are given at the end of the annex). The PPO will receive three
months of training abroad in relevant institutions and countries. In addition,
four inspectors - one in each region - will assist the district and thana
agricultural officers in field supervision.
5.         Content:  The agricultural assistants would be trained in popula-
tion problems and motivation techniques at the thana level by the thana
agricultural officers in cooperation with thana family planning officers and
guest lecturers. The assistants would then talk to the farmers contacted
during their visit to the villages about the relationship of agricultural
development and population growth both at the national and familial levels.
These agents would then submit a brief monthly report on farmers' attitudes,
reactions and main problems in accepting family planning.  A special kit
containing written instructions and flip charts will be given *to each agent
as well as a slide projector and a bicycle.
6.         Administration:  The PPO will prepare the detailed plans for the
execution of the scheme.  Ile will arrange for preparation of training material
and provision of slides. The district and thana agricultural officers in
pilot areas will receive orientation in population programs in Dacca for a
week.  The ten agricultural assistants of each thana would receive training
for about two weeks in the first year and one week reorientation every year
at the thana level bv the thana officers and guest lectujrers.
7.         Coverage:  One thana in eacii clistrict (19) will be covered by the
pilot scheme in a phased manner over a tlhree-year period. Ten tlhanas (four
concentrated and six others) will be undertaken in the first year and the
rest of the nine in the second year.  The thanas selected for this scheme
will be the same as those selected for the mothers' clubs scheme under tlhe
Mlinistry of Labor and Social Welfare.
S.         Expected Testults:  It is expected that each agricultural assistant
will motivate about ten farners in each village per year.  No less than
19,000 persons in the 1,900 villages in the 19 thanas are likely to accept
family planning. This may mean about 57,000 acceptors in the three-year
period.
12.        E.valuations:  While the external. evaluation of the schemes will
he condtucted by the PPS at the Planning Commission the internal evaluation
within the Min1stry would consist of regular reporting and special studies
in collaboration with the l'PD at the MOIIPP.



ANNEX 1 1
Page  3
(a)  Regular Reporting:  Monthly reports will be prepared by the
agricultural assistants giving information on:  (i) the number
of farmers who were contacted to talk about agriculture and
population, and (ii) the number of times the special kit and
slide projector were used; and the number of adults who
attended the shows. The reports then are sent to the thanas
where additional union information is provided on: (i) the number
of agents required to be in position, (ii) the number actually
in position, (iii) the number trained under the scheme, and
(iv) the number of agents supplied with the special kits and slide
projectors. Thana agricultural offices will send monthly
reports giving union data mentioned above to the district
office and headquarters, with copies to the PPD. They will
also send brief reports on the maintenance of the slide
projectors and other observations made during their inspection
visits to the agents.
(b) Special Studies: Funds would be provided to the Ministry
of Agriculture by the PPD for special studies on: (i) the
effectiveness of training given to thana agricultural officers
(evaluated at Dacca) and assistants (evaluated at thana),
(ii) the number and percentage of the assistants trained,
by thanas, (iii) the number and percentage of trained assistants
given kits and slide projectors by thana, and (iv) the frequency
of equipment use and number of adults who attended the shows.
Further internal evaluation should be made through studies
suggested under the mothers' club'scheme for the Ministry
of Labor and Social Welfare.
III. Staff and Other Requirements
9.        Personnel
(a) One population program officer (PPO) and the study
tour abroad for the PPO.
(b) Four inspectors - one in each region for field
supervision.
(c) One statistical assistant at the headquarters to assist
the population program officer in internal evaluation.
(d) One stenographer at headquarters.
(e) One driver and one guard/peon.



ANNTEX 11
Page 4
10.       Eauipment
(a)  One bicycle for each agriculture assistant in pilot
areas.
(b)  One bicycle for each thana agricultural officer for
supervision.
(c)  Slide projectors (19) - one for each thana for audio-
visual support for training and talks to the farmers.
(d)  Office equipment and kit bags (flip charts and
slides, portable slide projector and portable
tape recorder) one per assistant.
(e)  Camra and spare parts for production and slides.
tt.       Operating Costs:  Travel and per diems expenses; funds for main-
tenance of vehicles and internal evaluation.
12.       Work Schedule:

BANGLADESH
POPULATICON PROJ.CT
Pcpulation Proram of the MLnist.y of Education
1.        This annex describes the existing system of education that can
be used for the introduction of population education both for the school
children and the community outsi4e, the proe4  orization at the Ministry
for the purpose (see organizational chart 94, specific schemes for introduc-
tion of population education, the facilities proyided in the project for these
schemes and the work schedule.
I.  Ongoing Ropgram
2.        The school system in  ang4e h is    fge-_-old respected institution.
Illiterate villagers valueie`ucation and-respect choo  teaehers as-the
symbol of learninig.  The schools, therefore, have a great potential for
generating measures for rural development.  There are about 35,594 primary
schools and about 5,039 high schools ii the country.  The estimated 130,000
primary and 80,000 secondarty school teachers are generally recognized as
key resources in the rural are4s.  They represent an elite that can legitimize
developmental projects and programs.  UNICEF, for example, has trained
9,000 primary school teachers in health, sanitation and nutrition.  In addition
to the schools 'themselves, the 48 primary teacher training institutes, the
six secondary school teachers'  training institutes and the Education Extension
Center at Dacca arrange for the orientation an  training of school techers.
3.        The Education Commission has recogni,zp4ed the importance of popula-
tion education and has recommended the formation  of a National Committee
to study the: introduction of population education in the school system.
The Institut,e of E4ucation Research, Dacca Unt*prSity, is being assisted
by the Ford Foundation for the development of population education material.
This-material will be studied in 4n schools in 1975 on a pilot basis.
rleanwhile, the Directorate of Public Instructions is proposing to initiate
the work on curricul,um development through its Curriculum Development
Committee. 'It is intended that the findings of the studies conducted by
the Institute of Educational Research will be used in the process of
the final revision of text books.
4.        The project includes the following to support the above described
activities in population education:



AkYREX 12
Page 2
(a) A mobile population education team to conduct seminars
on population problems for primary and secondary school
teachers in each pilot thana, to be arranged by the
Education Extension Center.
(b) Development of population education material for
curriculum development through the Directorate of
Public Instructions.
(c) National seminars on population education to be
organized by the Institute of Educational Research,
Dacca University.
II. Organization for Population Education
5.        A Population Program Officer (PPO), at the level of Deputy Director,
nucleus of all population-related activities in the Ministry of Education,
will be appointed in the Directorate of Public Instruction. He will report
to the Director, Public Instructions. He will have supporting staff and will
be specifically responsible for the implementation of the proposed schemes
in the Ministry of Education. The PPO, will receive three months' training/
orientation abroad in those countries where population education has reached
an advanced stage. The PPO will be assisted by an adviser in the detailed
preparatiot of the scheme. Although the PPO will be mainly responsible for
population education curriculum development, he will also assist in the
proposed pilot scheme for the mobile population education team. For the pilot
scheme a seminar coordinator and a lecturer are provided separately. (The
terms of reference of the PPO and adviser are given at the end of this annex.)
III. Mobile Population Education Team For Seminars on
Population Problems for Primary and Secondary
School Teachers in Pilot Thanas
6.        Objective:  The main objectives is to seek the cooperation and
support of teachers for the family planning program and elicit their co-
operation for family planning motivation of the immediate community, through
special seminars on population problems.
7.        Content:  A lecturer, along with a coordinator, would visit the pilot
thana twice a year for about a week to conduct seminars for teachers from
primary and secondary schools.  The seminars will cover different aspects
of population problems and ways and means of solving the problems. One
teacher from each school from the pilot thanas will be selected. Teachers
in groups of 50 will be invited to thana headquarters for the seminars. The



f XX 12
Page 3
seminar discussions will be based on background papers to be prepared by
the staff in the first instance. Written papers from participants would be
invited for discussions in subsequent seminars.
8.        Coverage:  On an average there may be 1,700 primary schools and
over 200 secondary schools in the 19 pilot thanas or about 86 primary and
12 secondary schools in each thana. One teacher from each of these schools
will be invited for the seminars.
9.        Expected Results:  On an average there is one school for two
villages. It is expected that at least 50% of the villages in each thana
where the primary school teachers lives would be influenced by his opinion.
Therefore, about 1,000 villages out of about 1,900 in 19 pilot thanas will
be covered. Assuming only five acceptors per year per village through the
influence of primary school teachers, about 15,000 acceptors are expected to
be recruited in three years.
10.       Administration:  An officer in charge of arranging the seminar
(coordinator), would be appointed at the Education Extension Center. He will
report to the Director of the Education Extension Center. A lecturer would assist
in the actual organization and evaluation of seminars. The lecturer would
be given orientation by the PPO and the Coordinator. The coordinator would
also obtain the necessary film from the Ministry of Information and Broad-
casting and the Ministry of Health and Population Planning or Family Planning
Association and produce the slides needed to support the seminars. The
schedule and content of seminars, discussions, and background papers will be
prepared by the lecturer. The driver would be trained in the use of audio-
visual equipment and in simple repairs. Supervision of the seminars will
be undertaken by the PPO. He would check at least half the seminars for
the organizational content and effectiveness every year.
11.       Evaluations:           While the external evaluation will be conducted
by the PPS at the Planning Commission the internal evaluation would consist
of regular reporting and special studies in collaboration with the PPD at
MCHPP.
(a)  Regular Reorting: The coordinator would keep a record
of the number of teachers who attended the seminar.
Also, he would administer some simple before and
after questions to the participants to assess (i) the
content of background papers and talks, and (ii) the
audiovisual aids.   The coordinator would report on
the results, make the analysis and send them to the
PPO and PPD every quarter.
(b) The coordinator would arrange for special studies to
evaluate the effectiveness of the seminars in terms



'fNMEX 72
Page 4
of (i) its impact on knowledge, attitude and practice
of family planning, and (ii) the influence of the
teachers in the community and to what extent population-related
information was conveyed and what total impact was made.
Staff and Other Requirements
12.       Personnel
(a) One coordinator to organize and schedule the seminar;
(b) One lecturer whose primary function would be to
deliver lectures on population problems and help in
preparing the discussion materials for seminars;
(c) Two drivers and one clerk-typist; and
13.       Vehicles and Equipment:
(a) two four-wheel drive vehicles for the mobile
population education team,
(b) one motion-picture projector and one slide
projector for audiovisual aid, and
(c) office equipment.
13.       Operating Costs:
(a) Allowances for teacher participants; and
(b)  Cost of maintenance of vehicles, special equipment
and the production of printed material.
14.       Work Schedule:
(a) Appointment of coordinators and lecturers for
mobile population education;                              July 1975
(b)  Procurement of equipment and vehicles;                    July 1975
(c)  Training of lecturer and production of material; and   August 1975
(d)  Evaluation of the 10 thanas;                              December 1976
(e)  Extension of the scheme to the remainder of the nine   January -
thanas; and                                              February 1977
(f)  Final evaluation of the 19 thana schemes                  December 1978



ANNEX 12
