Cost
15.       The total cost of the scheme is US$148,000.  The details are given
in the table at the end of this annex.
IV. Curriculum Development
16.       Objective:  To initiate the long-term effort in the introduction
of population education in the school system through development and training
of teachers.
17.       Contents:  Three committees would be formed for curriculum devel-
opment in population education for primary, secondary and higher secondary
schools.  These three committees would hold about eighty meetings to
discuss and develop the first draft of the curriculum. Teachers from
secondary school, from the Secondary School Teachers Training College, and
Primary School Teachers Training Institutes would be trained for a week
in the population education material developed by the committees. Such
training would help in testing the curriculum, as well as in initiating the
process of preparing the teachers for the revision of text books.
18.       Coverage:  The scheme would train at least one teacher from all
the secondary schools, the Secondary School Teachers Training College and the
superintendent of Primarv School Teachers Training Institutes. Over 7,000
teachers would be trained during the three-year project period.
19.       Expected Results:  The scheme is likely to generate interest in
population problems among the 7,000 teachers at least. It will also help in
setting up the first step towards the long process of text hook revision
which may be completed by 1980.
20.       Administration:  The Population Program Officer, as mentioned in
Section II of this annex would be responsible for arranging the meeting
of the Curriculum Development Committee, for production of population
education material and the training of teachers. The Director of Public
Instruction will supervise the curriculum development and training of teachers.
21.       Evaluations:  While the external evaluation will be conducted by
the PPS of the Planning Commission, the internal evaluation will consist of
regular reporting and special studies in collaboration with the PPD at the
MOHPP.
(a) Regular Reporting. The PPO would submit progress reports
on the committees' work, the number of teachers trained by
type of school and subjects they teach. The reports will
be submitted to the PPD with copies to the Director of
Public Instructions and the Education Extension Center.



ANNEX 1 2
Page   6
(b) Special Studies. The PPO would arrange for special studies
through sample surveys of teachers undergoing training
before and after the one-week course to assess: (i) the
effectiveness of material produced by the committees;
(ii) content of training of teachers; and (iii) mode of
dissemination of information.
Staff and Other Requirements
22.       Personnel:
(a) Population program officer (PPO) to coordinate and follow-up
the population education program:
(b) Adviser to assist the PPO and the study tour abroad for the PPO;
(c) Two clerks; and
(d) Two drivers.
23.       Vehicle:
(a) Two four-wheel drive vehicles for the population
program officer's work and for the committee's work.
24.       Operating Costs:
(a) Cost of maintenance of vehicles, special eauipment
and the production of printed material; and
(b)  Allowances for committee members for the revision
of curriculum.

VII. National Seminar on Population Education
26.       Objective:  To call public attention to the need for population
education among the young school-age population, gain official support
for it and discuss priority approaches to the problem.
27.       Content:  The national seminar will draw participants (teachers
and experts in the field) from remote areas in the country. The discussion
will be on the need, content, and form of population education to be
introduced in the school system.
28.       Administration:  The Institute of Educational Research, Dacca
University will organize the conference under the joint sponsorship of the
Education Extension Center and Directorate of Public Instruction.
29.       Requirements:
(a)  Honoraria, travel, per diem expenses for 200 participants;
(b)  Funds for printing and publication of papers.
30.       Expected Results:  The conference is seen as an essential step
in the process of advising the Government on developing an effective
national population education program.
31.       Internal Evaluation:  The Institute of Educational Research will
analyze the achievetients of the seminar and determine the required follow-up
measures.

BANGLADESH
POPULATION PROJECT
Terms of Reference for the Population Program Officer of the Ministry
of Education
1.        The population program officer will be responsible for integration
of population control programs in the the Ministry's ongoing activities and
for the implementation of the pilot schemes. In particular, he will have
the responsibility for:
(a) Keeping liaison with the PPD and the PPS;
(b)  Submitting quarterly reports to the PPD;
(c) Arranging for the work of the Curriculum Development
Committee;
(d) Arranging for internal evaluation of the scheme
analysis of routine data and feedback of the results
of evaluation to the staff of the scheme and the Director
of Public Instruction ;
(e) Feedback of the results of evaluation to the field staff;
(f) Making suitable modification in the scheme based on
the results of evaluation;
(g) Ensuring effective supervision of the scheme and
making field visits for supervision of pilot scheme.
Qualifications
2.        Preferably a senior civil servant from the ministry concerned.



ANlNEX 12
Appendix II
Page 1
BANGLADESH
POPULATION PROJECT
Terms of Reference of Population Education Adviser of the MLinistry of Education
1.        To assist the Ministry of Education in the development of population
education through:
(a) Advice to senior officials in the Ministry of Education
on the broad spectrum of population education.
(b) Assistance in developing staff and committee mechanisms for
the continuing activity of coordinating and planning groups,
subject work groups, and ad hoc groups on special topics.
(c) Advice to professionals in education to help determine specific
emphasis, age and grade levels for the several areas of
content comprising education on population problems.
(d) Assistance to curriculum committees for various school levels in
preparing syllabus material, reading and reference lists,
tape recordings and related instructional aids.
(e) Consulting with officials of the several teacher training
institutions on building population education components
into the basic teacher education curricula.
(f) Assistance to the population program officer in development of
educational material for the mobile population education team
and for the teachers' seminar in pilot thanas.
2.        Qualifications:
High academic qualifications (preferably Master's degree in
education or behavioral sciences) with experience in education planning,
curriculum development and in managing population education or related
programs.



ANNEX 13
Page   1
BANGLADESHI
POPULATION PROJECT
Population Program of the Ministry of Information and Broadcasting
1.        The Departments of the Ministry of Information and Broadcasting
most concerned with population are Radio Bangladesh, Mfass Communications,
Press Information and, eventually, the Films Department. Television is not
yet considered to be of great importance as its signals are confined to the
Dacca area and there are very few receiving sets. This annex describes
the existing facilities for ongoing programs in these departments of the
Ministry, summarizes the proposed organization at the Ministry to plan and
coordinate population program efforts and outlines the individual schemes
to support the population program information (see organizational chart 9410).
At the end a note on overall evaluation of the Mlinistry's program is also added.
I. Ongoing Program
2.        Radio Bangladesh:  Approximately, 600,000 radio sets are reDorted
in the country and each set supposedly covers about 50 persons.   Therefore,
about 30 million persons are estimated to be radio listeners at present.
Different nation building programs are transmitted on the radio for the rural
population. During the War of Independence radios were an important channel
of communication. In support of the Government's goal of increasing food
production Bangladesh Radio has given renewed attention to agricultural broad-
casting. A daily one-hour program at prime listening time features experts
in all phases of agriculture and includes sufficient entertainment value to
to appeal to audiences. The logs indicate that some programs on family planning
have been broadcast. The Dacca station has a daily schedule of fourteen to
fifteen hours of broadcasting. In addition there is a network of five medium
wave transmitting stations at Rajshashi, Rangpur, Chittagong, Khulna and
Sylhet. Radio Bangladesh enjoys good credibility among rural people. Prime
listening time in rural areas is from 1900 to 2000 hours and for urban
audiences 2100 to 2300 hours. It is uncertain how many of the radio receivers
are worklni due to lack of spare parts and batteries.
3.        Mass Communications:  This department shows films through a fleet
of fifty-six mobile vans and organizes talks and group meetings. It also
has about 90 Public Relations Officers working. at headquarters and in the
field. Of these, 18 are district public relations officers supervising the
work of 70 sub-division PROs and these are already doing some family
planning information work.



ANNEX 13
Page 2
4.        Department of Films:  This is a large department.  Among a staff
of 118 people, 55 are engaged in film production. At the moment, no
laboratory and processing is done through the Film Development Corporation
which is already overloaded with commercial production (250 feature films
a year) and this causes grave delays in the production work of the Films De-
partment. This is particularly serious in the field of news reels. The news
reels and documentaries are made on 35 mm film and are shown in over 200 com-
mercial cinema halls and 70 mobile units. The showing of these films is
compulsory and the Department makes 20 copies of each film to circulate from
cinema to cinema. The cinema is extremely popular in Bangladesh as it is
in the rest of the sub-continent and wherever possible the films all have a
strong emotional content. Until now the Department has concentrated on
cinema exhibition since the reduction to 16 mm facilities are inadequate and
the Department considers that projectors of commercial cinemas are less lilcely
to break dovn than official 16 mm distribution. The films inform and educate
about national events and the progress and development made in different
sectors of national life. Professionally the quality of the films is very
good.
5.        Press Information Department:  This department helps in disseminating
information through feature articles, personal interviews, stories, poems,
short dramas in newspapers, periodicals and magazines as well as providing
material for radio and television.
6.        The project will make use of the work of the four departments de-
scribed above on a pilot basis as well as by giving general program support.
The pilot scheme, in the Department of Mass Communication, is for a wider
and more intensive use of audiovisual vans for showing films on population
problems.
7.        The general support consists of:
a.   establishing a Population Planning Cell in Radio
Bangladesh,
b.   support to the Department of Films so that they can
overcome the laboratory bottle-neck and enlarge their
production staff and equipment for production of family
planning films in both 35 mm and 16 mm to strengthen
the population program,
c.   setting up a Population Feature Writers Bureau which
will provide regular material for the press in general,
written in a style to suit the public taste,
d.   training of 90 public relations officers in the population
program.



ANNEX 13
Page 3
II. Organization of the Population Program in the
Ministry of Information and Broadcasting
8.        The appointment of a population program officer (PPO) in the
Ministry at the level of the Deputy Director has been proposed. The PPO
should report directly to the Joint-Secretary of the Ministry. Since there
will be a pilot scheme and four general support schemes within the Ministry,
the role of the PPO will be important. The PPO will be particularly
responsible for the pilot scheme. An adviser for six man-months will assist
the PPO in detailed preparation and evaluation of the schemes. (The terms
of reference of the PPO and advisers are given in Appendix I.) An Evaluation
Unit at the Ministry has been established.
III. Pilot Scheme
Use of Mobile Cinema Vans
9.        Objective:  By using the powerful emotional impact of the film
a major motivational compaign will be launched to influence the public towards
family planning. At the same time a regular film contact will be maintained
with the public to inform and educate them on population problems and ways
and means of solving them.
10.       Content:  Pending local production by the Films Department selected
films from appropriate countries will be dubbed in Bengali. The Films De-
partment will produce a series of films on all aspects of the population
problem most of which will be made with a strong emotional appeal, but
there will be a few with a straight-forward informative nature. The audio-
visual vans will exhibit the films and some of them will give daylight
shows especially for those women who do not go out at night while
others will give evening shows for large audiences.  The vans wln also be
able to give more intimate showings of films on family planning techniques.
Since half the value of a motivational film show is in its presentation,
special attention will be given to the training of the PROs who will present
the films. They will also be responsible for providing feedback as to audience
reaction to the Ministry and Evaluation Unit of the PPD.
11.       Coverage:  The pilot scheme would cover all eight thanas (two
in each region) during the three-year implementation period. Only four con-
centrated thanas will be covered in the first year; the rest of the four
thanas in the second year.
12.       Expected Results:  About 150 shows by each mobile unit in a year
are expected to be arranged. With two mobile vans it would mean an average



ANNEX 13
Page 4
of 30 shows per month in a thana with about 100 villages having a total
population of around 180,000. The mobile vans would visit each village about
four times a year. It is not possible to estimate the number of persons
motivated to practice family planning as a result of these film shows.
13.       Administration:  The Department of M4ass Communications in colla-
boration with the Film Department will implement the pilot scheme. The
public relations officer would organize the programs in the field. The
PPO will have specific responsibility for the administration of the scheme.
An audiovisual engineer, along with the supporting staff, would help in super-
vising maintenance of all equipment in the project. Both the PPO and the
audiovisual engineer would receive training/orientation abroad for three
months each. While the former will visit communication research institutes
the latter will visit the countries and firms supplying the bulk of the
equipment to be maintained. The maintenance section of the Mass Communi-
cation Department will service the projectors for all the ministries.
14.       Evaluations:  While the external evaluation of the schemes will
be conducted by the PPS of the Planning Commission, the internal evalua-
tion within the Ministry would consist of regular reporting and special
studies in collaboration with the PPD at the MOHPP.
a.   Regular Reporting:  The operators will send to public
relations officers (PROs) monthly reports on (i) the number
of film shows put on in different areas, (ii) the number of
adult males and females who attended the shows, (iii)
types of questions asked after the show, and (v) the general
response to the shows. The PROs would consolidate the
reports by union, and add brief notes of their obser-
vations on maintenance of the equipment, organization of the
film shows, and response of the public to the shows. As
far as possible, about 15 persons from the audience should
be interviewed after the show to ascertain whether the
show conveyed the message clearly. Reports on such obser-
vations will be useful for revising the films or to give
adequate oral explanations on common points of doubt before
or after subsequent film shows. The PROs will send monthly
reports to the PPO at headquarters, who will circulate the
reports to concerned departments of the Ministry.
b.   Special Studies:  Fulnds would be provided to the Ministry
of Information and Broadcasting by the PPD for the following
special studies: (i) pre-testing of films for their effec-
tiveness (at headquarters), (ii) the number and percentage
of villages in which film shows are organized, in each union
of the thana, (iii) the estimated number of males and females
who attended the shows, by union, (iv) a quarterly review
at the thana and ministry levels of operators and PROs on
the organization of the film shows, and the response



ANNEX 13
Page  5
of the public to the film shows) with the purpose of
taking appropriate action to remedy deficiencies
either in the organization of the shows or in the films them-
selves. Additional evaluation studies are suggested at the
end of this annex.

V. Program Support
Establishing a Population Program Cell in Radio Bangladesh
29.       Objective:  To create a unit in Radio Bangladesh whose sole purpose
will be to ensure that sufficient program and air time for population and
family planning matters are available both at the Dacca station as well as
at the five other regional stations. This unit will be responsible for
producing programs of its own devising as well as influencing other producers
to introduce population/family planning themes into their own programs. It
will make sure that the material is presented in a manner that will appeal
to the public.
30.       Content:  The Ministry will give from 10-15 minutes each day of prime
time from the Dacca station which will be exclusively concerned with the
population program as well as ensuring that other programs contain suitable
population material inspired by the population program cell. The following
are some of the programs proposed:
a.   Pannel discussions and talks by experts on population
planning;



ANNEX 13
Page 7
b.   Features, short plays and local songs projecting themes
on population planning;
c.   Interviews with a cross section of people, particularly
those who are regular users of family planning methods;
O
d.   Documentary programs on various population planning units,
implementation bodies, centers and cells;
e.   Motivation songs and musical sketches on population
planning.
31.       Administration:  A director will be attached to Radio Bangladesh
for the development and broadcast of population programs. In each of the
six regional radio stations a producer will be appointed for ensuring the
production of programs with suitable local content and their regular
broadcast.
32.       Coverage:  The six stations, namely Dacca, Chittagong, Rajshahi,
Rangpur, Khulna and Sylhet cover 85% of the population. The programs will
be specially designed for adults as well as children.
33.       Expected Results:  Depending on the types of broadcasts and their
frequency, it is expected that a large section of the population will become
aware of population problems and of the Government's policies and programs.
34.       Evaluations:  The external evaluation will be conducted by the
PPS at the Planning Commission. The internal evaluation to be conducted
in collaboration with PPD at the MOHPP should be geared towards the listeners'
survey to determine the impact of various types of programs and suitability
of their timing. The results of internal evaluation should be readily fed
back to the producer for continuous program improvement.
a.   Regular Reporting:  Assistant regional directors will send
monthly reports to project headquarters on the number of
broadcasts put on regional radio by (i) category, (ii) theme,
(iii) duration, (iv) timing, (v) target population, (male or
female) and (vi) important participants, where appropriate.
b.   Special Studies:  A survey of radio listeners should
be undertaken to evaluate this scheme. (Details are
given at the end of this annex.)

Support of the Films Department
40.       Objective:  To use what is considered to be the most powerful mass
media - the film - for population and family planning motivation and educa-
tion. To this end films on population matters will be made in local set-
tings. In order that this program can be carried out the Film Department
will need extensive additional equipment in order to overcome laboratory
delays, to be able to convert its present 35 mm productions to 16 mm and to
undertake direct production of 16 mm training films. At the same time,
the staff will need to be increased as the present production team is already
overscheduled. The Film Department will put one film on population into imme-
diate production as part of its normal program. But since there will then
be a delay before there is regular production of films, arrangements will be
made to dub six carefully selected films from other appropriate countries.
Pending the installation of necessary equipment this work may have to be
done outside Bangladesh.
41.       Content:  Apart from the direct emotional-appeal films, some of
the themes on which films will be produced are as follows:
a.   General motivation to population planning in
relation to the special circumstances of Bangladesh;
b.   Population problem in relation to the food situation
of Bangladesh;



ANNEX 13
Page 10
c.   Population problem in relation to employment
and other economic resources of Bangladesh;
d.   Social-ills and vices and other social problems due
to over-population;
e.   Population problem in relation to the health problems
in the context of Bangladesh;
f.   Population problem in relation to the available and
potential educational facilities in Bangladesh;
g.   Education and demonstration of family planning
methods; and
h.   Technical education for implementation of family
planning program.
42.       Coverage:  A large section of the population over seven years
of age will be reached either through the 270 commercial cinemas or the
forty mobile projectors being purchased under this program or by the
fifty-six projectors already in use by the Mass Communications Depart-
ment. There are also other projectors in use in various places but these
have not as yet been surveyed.
43.       Expected Results:  Approximately 14 films with a total running
time of five hours will be produced during the three-year period; on an
average five films a year, although the production during the first year
may be less. Approximately 50% will be in color. There will also be one
feature-length film of approximately 100 minutes duration produced during
the second year. These films will be seen by the ordinary cinema goers many
of whom come from nearby rural areas and whose numbers are estimated at
roughly 500,000 a day. They will also be seen by means of the project's
own fleet of 59 projectors and here they will have the advantage of being
presented in a manner which it is hoped will make their effectiveness much
greater. All the films will be pre-tested before public exhibition.
44.       Administration:  The Director of the Department of Films, with
the assistance of a film producer, would be responsible for the administra-
tion of the program.
45.       Evaluations:  While the external evaluation will be done
by the PPS of the Planning Commission, the internal evaluation will be con-
ducted by the Evaluation Unit of the Ministry in collaboration with the PPD
at the MIOHPP. The simplest evaluation to be done routinely is in terms of
(i) production of various categories of films by target dates, and (ii) the
number of film shows presented in cinema halls and through open-air mobile
units compared to the targets set, year by year.   The themes for the films
and method of presentation for different types of population may be decided



ANNEX 13
Page 11
in consultation with experts in the field.   Equally important, if not more
important than this, is a quick audience survey before the films are finalized
and several copies made.   Appropriate sections of the population should
be shown the films to ascertain whether the important information which
each film purports to convey is adequately and clearly conveyed or not, and,
more importantly, to ensure that the films do not unintentionally convey
wrong ideas. While showing the films in final form, the audiences should
be requested to give their views regarding the content, presentation, timing,
etc., of the films.   Suggestions from the public should be taken into serious
consideration while reviewing the film production program. Other evaluation
studies required are given at the end of this annex.

c.   One scriptwriter;

If necessary a consultant will be provided for two or three months to advise
on the necessary technical approaches to the production of training films.

negatives, for reducing 35 mm film to 16 mm,-sound
recording equipment for 16 nm production, and extra
35 mm and 16 mm camera equipment.

foreign films, for maintenance of vehicles and special equipment.

Setting up a Feature Writing Bureau
51.       Objective:  Dissemination of information on the population program
through publication of articles, features, personal interviews, stories, poems,
short drama, cartoons, etc. in newspapers, periodicals and magazines and
through radio and television broadcasts.
52.       Contents:  The Feature Waiting Bureau which is to be established
under the Press Information Department will prepare material on the population
problem for publication as well as for broadcast. The Bureau will maintain
regular contact with the Population Planning Division, Bangladesh Institute
of Development Studies, Health Division of IOHPP, Planning Commission and
other ministries for the collection of material from which suitable themes
on population planning will then be prepared and supplied to journalists,
authors, poets, literatures, economists, etc. to write articles, features,
stories, poems, short dramas, etc. on a honorarium basis. The cooperation
of journalists will also be enlisted to interview various cross-sections of
the people and to write personal reviews from them. The Bureau will then
edit them, select cartoons or photographs for their illustration and release
them for publication through the Press. Cartoons showing the negative effects
of large families and over-population on our social and economic life can also
be regularly published through newspapers and periodicals.
53.       Coverage:  The literate urban population will be covered through
the press and a large part of the illiterate rural-urban population will
be covered through radio and cartoons.
54.       Expected Results:  On an average four articles, four features, four
personal interviews, three stories, three poems, one short drama and six
cartoons will be published or broadcast/telecasted in a month.
55.       Administration:  The head of the Press Information Bureau will be
responsible for the administration of the program. He will have additional
staff consisting of feature writers, artists, etc. specifically for this
program.



AINEX 1 3
Page 14
56.       Evaluations:  The external evaluation will be done by the PPS
at the Planning Commission. The internal evaluation to be done in collaboration
with PPD at the MIOHPP should assess the impact of articles, dramas, features
or cartoons by inviting comments and suggestions of readers.

Training of Public Relations Officers
62.       Objective:  To orient the public relations officers (information
officers) of the Ministry on the motivational aspects of the population
programs. There are 90 PROs and in the field they will be responsible
for supporting all program activities that concern the general public.
63.       Content:  Initially a fifteen-day orientation course will be
provided at Dacca for groups of 15-20 officers at a time. Subsequently
reorientation courses will be arranged in the second and third years of
the program. The topics to be covered will range from the statement
of the population problem to various communication techniques. Since
the major communication media used in the project is the film, special emphasis
will be given to presenting film shows in the most effective way and follow-
up after the show has ended.
64.       Coverage:  All 90 public relations officers (PROs) will receive
orientation training during the first year of operation of the schemes.
Priority in orientation will be given to the PROs in the pilot. thanas.
65.       Administration:  The Director of the Department of Mass Communi-
cation will be responsible for the implementation of the program with the



Z2SNN.EX 13
Page1 6
assistance o. one coordination and training officer.  Rei.ance will be
placed on guest lecturers for actual training.
66.       Evaluations:  The external evaluation will be done by the PPS at
the Planning Commission. The internal evaluation to be conducted in colla-
boration with the PPD at the INOHPP will assess the effectiveness of training
given to the PROs by administering tests, before and after training to
measure the improvement in their knowledge of population problems and
communication techniques. The training program of each groups will be
evaluated to determine the understanding of the problem. Further follow-up
of the PROs' activities will be achieved by assessing the operational impact
on the training.

Overall Evaluation of the Additional Facilities in the Ministry
of Information and Broadcasting
72.       For evaluating the five projects of the Ministry based on the
routine reports and special surveys suggested, there should be an evaluation
unit in the Ministry. With the exception of the training scheme for PROs,
the remaining four can adequately be evaluated only through special surveys.
It is suggested that a comprehensive survey be undertaken by about the end
of 1975 or mid-1976 to evaluate together the activities of the four schemes.
73.       One rural and one urban sample should be taken for the survey.
The scheme, namely, audiovisual (AV) vans, would operate in rural parts of
eight thanas (two in each district), while the remaining three schemes cover
the entire country. Four thanas, two concentrated and two other pilot thanas
in which the above-mentioned scheme operates, should be selected. These
should be in the four regions of the country, and therefore, in four dif-
ferent districts. Four other thanas also should be selected from these
districts. Of the remaining districts, one should be selected from each
region, and within each of the selected districts two accessible thanas
should be selected. Thus, the survey should cover 16 thanas in eight districts
- two districts from each region. From these 16 thanas, a rural sample of
about 1,200 households should be drawn, and all married males and females in
the households should be interviewed with the assistance of a questionnaire.
A separate sample of 1,200 urban households in the four regions should also
be included in the survey. These samples would provide data for comparison
of the scheme effects on married males and females in urban areas where
only the three schemes operate, as well as in rural areas in which all four
sclhemes operate.
74.       The interview questionnaire should include in addition to others,
the following important questions (where appropriate), relating to the five
schemes to be evaluated:
a.   AV vans:  Whetlier a van visited the area and, if
visited, whether the respondent attended or learned
about this show; if attended, his/her response and
suggestions regarding organization of the show, the
contents and presentation.



ANNEX 3 3
Page 1 8
b.   Radio Program:  Whether the household owns or haas ready
access to a radio; respondent's radio listening habits
or preference regarding frequency, timing and types of
programs; any radio program relating to population heard
during the month preceding interview; if heard,identifica-
tion of program and station and when; information
respondent got from each program; respondent's views
about the clarity, trustworthiness/authenticity of
information, on the timing, duration and frequency of each
type of program heard.
c.   Films:  Respondent's overall frequency of going to movies
and number of times during the last two months; any film
relating to population seen during the last two months;
if seen, what was the message and what was the respondent's
view about the clarity of message, etc.
d.   Feature Writing:  Respondent's general reading habits;
whether respondent has read (or heard about) any of the
Ministry's publications; if read (or heard about the
contents) respondent's grasp of important points from
each publication; respondent's comments and suggestions.
75.       The project provides for one Evaluator (Social Scientist) and two
statistical assistants, and two calculators for internal evaluation of all
schemes of the Ministry based on routine reports. In addition, a provision
is made for an evaluation survey to be conducted in 1975 either by the
Ministry itself or by contracting out to a suitable research institution.
Evaluation of the films would be based on personal interviews after the films
have been shown in selected movie theaters.

AN7NEL I
Appendix I
BANGLADESH
POPULATION PROJECT
Terms of Reference of the Population Program Officer at the
Ministry of Information and Broadcasting
1.        The population program officer will be responsible for:
a.   keeping liaison with the PPD and the PPS;
b.   submitting regular reports to the PPD;
c.   arranging for an orientation program for the staff working
on different sections of the plan;
d.   arranging for internal evaluation of the results of the
five different sections;
e.   ensuring that the evaluation feedback of the schemes
is transmitted to the different sections so that they
may improve their programs accordingly; and for
f.   coordinating the work of the four departments so that
all messages transmitted are compatible and that they follow
an overall family planning line to obtain maximum effect.
Communication Adviser(s) at the Ministry of Information and Broadcasting
2.        Provision is made for an adviser in case of need and depending
on the qualifications of the information officer chosen. At this point it
would not be sensible to outline the role of the adviser. In addition to
the adviser one can foresee the possible need for expert consultants for
short-term visits at specified moments. Help may be needed with installing
the film processing laboratories. Radio Bangladesh might require outside
advice on the maximum use of population broadcasts in rural areas.



Page 1
BANGLADESH
POPULATION PROJECT
Family Planning Motivation Program of the Yinistry
of Health and Population Planning
I. Ongoing Program
1.        The Ministry of Health and Population Planning has a plan to extend
simple health and family planning services to the rural population through
a team of family welfare workers (one male and one female). The female
counterpart will concentrate on the maternal and child health and family
planning program (see Annex 7). She will have a dual role: the delivery
of family planning services, and face-to-face education and motivation.
The Ministry, with WHO support, plans to provide a kit containing inocula-
tion and vaccination equipment, malaria control, simple medicine, etc.,
for every family welfare worker - men and women. To provide the needed
support for the education and motivation program, the project includes a
pilot scheme for the use of motivation kits by the Female Family Welfare
Workers (FFWW).
11. Use of Motivation Kit by the Female Family Welfare Worker
2.        Objective:  To test the effectiveness and practicability of audio-
visual support to the motivation effort of the FFWWs. These multi-purpose
workers will have so many responsibilities that family planning is likely
to receive low priority unless the worker is provided with resources that
make the work interesting.
3.        Content:  A special test demonstration kit will be provided to the
FFWWs in the pilot areas; their male counterparts will be allowed the use
of these kits. These kits will contain a battery-operated (flashlamp)
film slide projector, flip ciarts and a cassette tape player which will play
back prerecorded programs containing entertainment as well as motivational
messages. The key to the successful use of these kits is the production
of the tapes, slides and flip books which should be made with the target
audience firmly in mind. It is also important that the workers are well
trained in presenting the film slides in a stimulating manner. Local
conditions may, however, make the contents of the kits too cumbersome for
everyday use. If this is so then another form of support for motivational
work will need to be found.



KX ' 4_
z  2
4,            E       In all nineteen thanas (one in each district) will be
selected for the use of motivation kits. Ten thanas (four concentrated and
six others) will be covered in the first year and nine others in the second
year.
5.        Expected Results:  It is expected that the FFWWs will contact
women in the reproductive ages in the pilot thanas at least several times.
On an average, the FFWWs are expected to recruit 40 acceptors per village
per year. If the performance of FFWWs with kits improves, the average may
increase to 45 acceptors per village per year. This would mean an additional
3,000 acceptors in four years.
6.        Administration:  The MCH/FP Division of the Ministry, along with
TREC, will be responsible for the implementation of the program.  The thana
family planning officers will supervise the work.
7.        Evaluations:  While the external evaluation of the schemes will
be conducted by the PPS, the internal evaluation within the Ministry would
consist of regular reporting, periodic evaluations and special evaluation
studies.
(a) Regular Reporting: Under the procedures presently followed
in the family planning program of the MOHPP, all FFWWs sub-
mit a daily report on home visiting to the assistant in-
spector. She should furnish additional information on the
use of the kit in the same report on: (i) whether kit was
taken and used during the visit; (ii) if used, the number
of adult males and females that attended the demonstrations.
The assistant inspector who supervises Fn.Vs work, will pre-
pare a brief monthly report on the maintenance of the kit,
and organization of demonstrations. He will attach this to
the monthly report on family planning he prepares, based on
the daily reports of the FFWWs. The assistant inspector
sends the monthly report through the inspector, thana health
center, district office, to the MOHPP.
(b) Periodic Evaluation: A simple evaluation is completed at the
thana health center by the THOIIPP, in terms of feasibility
and frequency of kit use, and increasc in the number of
new family planning acceptors from the area of each FFWW
given a kit in comparison to the new acceptors in similar
areas in the thana.
III. Facilities
8.        Kits which include battery-operated tape recorders, slide pro-
jectors and flip charts.

BANGLADESH
POPULAtION PROJECT
System of Evaluation
I. Introduction
1.        This annex summarizes the general system of evaluation of the popu-
lation program to be established in Bangladesh. It focuses particularly on
the method of evaluation of the total program, the individual components,
the agencies to be responsible for each evaluation activity and its timing.
Details of evaluation of the pilot schemes for information, education and
communication and the collection of data on acceptors through service statis-
tics are discussed in separate annexes.
2.        Objective:  The objective of the system of evaluation is to
establish a mechanism for generating data for measuring (a) the changes in
fertility, and (b) the effectiveness of various program measures adopted to
achieve the changes in fertility.
3.        Indices of Performance:  The changes in fertility are to be
measured through age-specific fertility and total fertility rates. These
data, as proposed below, would be obtained mainly through surveys but could
also be estimated from vital registration and family planning acceptors'
records depending on their completeness. The effectiveness of various pro-
gram components such as delivery of services, training and information and
the education program would be measured finally in terms of changes in knowl-
edge, attitude and practice towards family planning. The data are to be
obtained through a small specialized survey and records of family planning
acceptors. But an important part of the evaluation of program inputs would
be the assessment (at an intermediary stage) of the operations of program
components, such as the pilot schemes, training of health and family plan-
ning persoDnel and delivery of service, etc. For this assessment, a system
of regular reporting will be established.
4.        Organization:  While the Health and Population Planning Section
(PPS) of the Planning Commission would be responsible for external evalua-
tion, the Population Planning Division (PPD) of the MDHPP would be respon-
sible for assisting the concerned ministries in internal evaluation and
in collating the results. The PPS will have an Evaluation Unit with core
staff to conduct certain evaluation studies and will have funds to contract
out other studies to various universities and research institutes, such as
the Bangladesh Institute of Development Studies, the Institute of Statistical
Research and Training, Dacca University, and the Universities of Chittagoag,
Rajshashi and Mymensingh. The regular reporting and internal evaluation



.age 2
w3ld be com&uc>ed by the  plaementing ministries which woud collect informa-
tion and send the regular reports to the PPD for analysis. These ministries
would also be responsible for feedback of the evaluation results to the staff
and improvements in the operations of the scheme. The PPD has enough man-
power and other resources to handle the additional work and the PPS is estab-
lishing the Evaluation Unit for this purpose.  (Details of facilities for
this section are given at the end of this annex.)  While the system of eval-
uation (objective, method, agency and timing) is summarized below and elab-
orated in later sections the key studies and their schedule is given in
Appendix I.
A.   Fertility change to be measured through:
(a) a demographic survey to be conducted by the Bangladesh
Institute of Development Studies (BIDS) and the Insti-
tute of Statistical Research and Training (ISRT) in
1977 or 1978 and to be followed up every three years;
(b) Analysis of vital statistics being collected by the
Inspection Directorate of the MOHPP in conjunction
with small fertility surveys; and
(c)  Estimates of family planning acceptors and their
characteristics to be collected by regular service
statistics of the MOHPP and small family planning
surveys.
B.   Evaluation of each component of population program to be conducted through:
(a) Internal evaluations by the ministries participating
in the program and the PPD consisting of:
Mi)  regular reports on the scheme;
(ii)  specific studies to measure various indices
of success of the scheme; and
(iii)  an analysis of regular reports supplied by
various ministries;
(b) External evaluation by the PPS consisting of periodic
surveys to be conducted by the PPS or contracted out
to other institutes or universities.
C.   Independent Review Team:
A team of expatriates and local experts to review the program after
the project is in operation for two years.



5
?age 3 ~
II. Measurement of Fertility Change
5.        Demographic Survey:  A post census enumeration survey is sched-
uled for completion by early 1975. This survey would be the baseline for
measuring changes in fertility through later surveys. A nationwide demo-
graphic survey, therefore, should be considered for 1977 or 1978. The PPS
should decide on the timing and feasibility of this survey as well as which
agency is likely to undertake it.
6.        Analysis of Vital Statistics:  The MOHPP (Health Division) has
already started on the couple registration scheme through the family welfare
workers (see Annex 17). The evaluation of data collected for this scheme
and its analysis is to be done by the Inspection Directorate (or similar
unit in the Health Division). However, the PPD would be supplied with the
analysis made by the Inspection Directorate. In the meantime, it should
conduct small special surveys to determine the levels of fertility and to
examine the completeness of the vital statistics information previously
collected. The PPD should then consider the need for establishing an alter-
native system of collection of vital rates.
7.        Acceptorst Records:  The MOHPP (both Health Division and PPD)
would have data on the number of family planning acceptors and their compo-
sition through the records to be maintained by family welfare workers. The
record of distribution of contraceptives through commercial channels and
other programs should be sent to the PPD for collection of all program sta-
tistics at one place. These data should be analyzed for demographic impact
by the PPD.
III. Evaluation of Program Components
A. Internal Evaluation
8.        The internal evaluation of the program has been discussed as part
of the program of six different ministries (see Annexes 9-14). Either each
ministry's existing evaluation unit is strengthened or separate additional
staff is provided for compilation of regular progress reports, its analysis
and feedback. Additional funds are also provided at the PPD for specific
studies to assess the effectiveness of the schemes.
(a) Regular Reports: The biggest program of internal
evaluation is that of the Ministry of Health and
Population Planning which includes collection of
service statistics. The project includes support for
analysis of service statistics and suggests methods
of improving the data. The details are given sepa-
rately in Annex 17. The Ministry of Local Government,



A2NEX 15
Page 4
Rural Development and Cooperatives has a well estab-
lished evaluation unit which, with additional facilities
provided in the project, is expected to deal with the in-
ternal evaluation. But statisticians are provided in the
project at headquarters to analyze the regular reports
to be received from thana staff. The regular reporting
in the Ministry of Agriculture will proceed through
the existing channel. Additional staff for compilation
of reports and for analysis and feedback is provided in
the project. No additional staff for analysis of regular
reports is provided in the Ministry of Education as the
population program officers and other staff in the scheme
will be responsible for it. The Ministry of Information
and Broadcasting will have a core staff for evaluation,
provided in the project, that would help in setting up
the system of regular reporting for all the schemes under
the Ministry. This core staff will also be responsible
for analysis and feedback of these reports.
(b) Specific Studies and Periodic Evaluation: The topic
for special studies are suggested for each scheme in
annexes dealing with the various ministries' programs.
But the population program officer in each ministry,
along with the adviser and the PPD, will decide on these
studies. The PPD and the ministry may give contracts to
the universities for such studies or employ special staff
to conduct them. Funds are allocated under the PPD budget
for special studies within each ministry.
B. External Evaluation
9.        All external evaluations of the different program components will
be the responsibility of the PPS. The external evaluation will focus on
variations among different thanas and among different villages in the same
thanas in: (a) management and administration of various schemes, (b' their
cost effectiveness, (c) impact on knowledge, attitude and practice of f-i  v
planning, and (d) the suitability of services provided to the consumers or
a survey of their choice to examine the causes for inadequate demand Jf scrv--
ices. The external evaluation will largely be conducted by its evaluation
unit which will receive full support from the project. The external evalua-
tion should cover each component of the program as described in the following
paragraphs.
10.       Service Delivery System:  Acceptor and non-acceptor surveys should
be conducted to assess the effectiveness of the service delivery system and
to find out to what extent the services rendered correspond to the demands
of the community. Furthermore, the relationship between non-acceptance and
non-availability of contraceptives, non-suitability of available methods,



Page 5
and administrative problems with government clinics and personnel should be
examined.
11.       Training:  The biggest cadre of personnel to be trained through
the project would be for the Health Division of the Ministry of Health and
Population Planning. Surveys on manpower utilization and on the functions
of family health visitors and family welfare workers should be conducted to
(a) assess the suitability of training, (b) assess the difference between
functions actually performed and required of them, and (c) find out more
efficient reallocations of functions.
12.       Information, Education and Communication Program:  A large part
of the information, education and communication (IEC) program is in the form
of pilot schemes. The pilot schemes will be tried in several geographic
areas (structure described in Annex 16). One thana from each of the 19 dis-
tricts will be selected for the operation of the 9 schemes in various combi-
nations.  The purpose of such a geographic distribution is to:
(a)  Assess the impact of individual schemes;
(b)  Analyze the administrative and other reasons for
regional variations in the success of different
schemes;
(c)  Assess the effect of cultural and social factors
on the success of the scheme; and
(d)  Assess the impact of all the schemes when in opera-
tion together.
In four thanas, seven of the nine schemes will be in operation. The purpose
of operating seven schemes in four thanas is to assess the impact of concen-
trated inputs on fertility behavior. In addition, operation of the schemes of
all different ministries in these concentrated thanas will reveal the admin-
istrative problem of coordination. The methodology and other details of
evaluation of pilot schemes in concentrated thanas and in other thanas are
given in Annex 16. Evaluation of the IEC program distinct from the pilot
schemes is discussed at the end of Annex 13.
13.       Evaluation:  How well the system of evaluation is working will be
examined by an Evaluation and Research Committee to be established by the PPS
and by the proposed review team (discussed below) through the assessment of
required information, the quality of data and the system of its feedback.
Review Team of the Population Program
14.       A team of experts will review the program sometime in 1978.  The
review team would consist of expatriates and local experts on:



Page 6
(a) Management and administration;
(b) Communications;
(c) Evaluation; and
(d) Maternal and child health and family planning.
15.       The terms of reference of the team will include:
(a) An up-to-date review of the progress made by the
program;
(b) An assessment of its possible demographic impact;
(c) A review of the effectiveness of individual com-
ponents of the program; and
(d) Suggested modifications for the program as a whole
and for individual components.
The project includes US$80,000 for this program review.
16.       The list of evaluation studies is given in Appendix II.
17.       Requirements:  The project provides the following funds and re-
quirements for the PPD and the PPS for program evaluation:
(a) Population Planning Division:
(i)  One evaluation and planning adviser to be used
by both the PPD and the PPS;
(ii)  Fellowship for a study tour abroad for the head
of the PPD; and.
(iii)  Funds for internal evaluation;
(b) Evaluation Unit of the Health and Population Planning
Section of the Planning Commission:
(i) Fellowship for a study tour abroad for the head
of the PPS;
(ii) Personnel:
a.   Two assistant chiefs (social scientists) for
designing evaluation studies and analyzing
results;



A sNNK15
Page 7
b.   Two supervisors for supervising data collection
in the field;
c.   Two statisticians to help with statistical
designs;
d.   Five statistical assistants to assist in com-
putation of data;
e.   Eight interviewers for field investigation;
f.   Two steno-typists; and
g.   Four drivers and one peon.
(iii)  Vehicles and Equipment:
a.   Four 4-wheel drive vehicles for supervision; and
b.   Five hand calculators, two electronic desk com-
puters and two typewriters.
(iv) Operating Costs:
a.   Vehicle maintenance and office supplies; and
b.   Funds for contracting out the evaluation
studies.
18.       Costs:  The detailed cost estimates are given in the table at
the end of this annex. The total cost of the facilities at the PPS is
estimated at US$481,800 and at the PPD, US$546,800.

Terms of Reference for the Planning and Evaluation Adviser
1.        To assist the heads of the PPS and the PPD in:
(a) Detailed planning of the pilot schemes and other
program components;
(b) Laying down the indices of performance of various
program inputs;
(c) Suggesting suitable methodology for evaluation of
different program components;
(d)  Setting up the system of coordination of reports
and flow of information; and
(e) Developing a system of analysis for the results
of evaluation and their feedback.
Qualifications
2.        An expert of established reputation in the field of population
program evaluation.

BANGLADESH
POPULATION PROJECT
Evaluation of the Pilot Schemes
1.        This annex briefly describes the objectives, methodology and agencies'
responsible for the evaluation of pilot schemes (Chart 9487). The evaluatiot
of pilot schemes will be by geographic areas and by schemes. The objectives
of the evaluation are described in Annex 15. The schemes will be evaluated
separately for four concentrated thanas and the rest of the thanas through
base-line and follow-up surveys during the project period. The major re-
sponsibility for the evaluation of these schemes will lie with the Evalua-
tion Unit of the PPS and the Evaluation Section of the PPD.
I. Surveys in the Four Concentrated Thanas
1.        The Institute of Statistical Research and Training (ISRT), an
autonomous organization of the University of Dacca, had, in the past, under-
taken several applied research studies in social science fields, including
demographic surveys and computer simulation studies of human fertility. It
has adequate facilities for coding, punching and computer analysis of data.
The Institute undertakes research studies sponsored by other agencies and
deputizes experienced staff to carry them out.
A. Base-line Survey
2.        Objective:  To determine bench-marks in terms of the extent of
knowledge, favorable attitudes and practice (KAP) relating to family plan-
ning, and the level of fertility for the population in the four thanas,
before the seven pilot schemes are started.
3.        Contents:  A representative sample of at least 2,500 currently
married women under 45 years of age will be selected from the four thanas
based on the couple registration data of the Ministry of Health and Popula-
tion Planning, or the 1974 population census data. A sub-sample of 1,000
of their husbands will also be included in Lhe survey. Wives will be inter-
viewed by females and husbands by males, preferably simultaneously but inde-
pendently. Wives and husbands will be interviewed with the help of separate
questionnaires. Both questionnaires will be pre-tested before they are fi-
nalized. Detailed instructions for answering the questionnaire will be
prepared. The wife's questionnaire will have two parts: (a) a household
section in which to list all members of the household by sex, age, marital



ANNEX 16
Page 2
status and their family relationships; and (b) a family planning and fertil-
ity section in which to give information on variables, such as the couple's
socio-economic background, marriage and fertility history; wife's attitudes
towards family size, child spacing, and adoption of family planning; knowl-
edge about family planning; past, current and expected future use of family
planning methods; and detailed pregnancy history in the past three years.
The husband's questionnaire will have items only on knowledge, attitude,
and practice of family planning. Based on detailed analysis of the data,
a report will be published and distributed to all persons concerned.
4.        Administration:  The survey will be conducted under the over-all
guidance of the Director of ISRT. The project provides for one full-time
Director and one Deputy Director. A Study Advisory Committee will be formed
consisting of representatives of the PPD, the PPS, important research insti-
tutions, and the Universities of Chittagong, Mymensingh, Rajshahi and Dacca.
Disciplines such as Statistics, Sociology, Psychology, Demography, Economics,
and health and family planning will be represented in the Committee. It will
advise on the design of the survey and report writing. Since one thana will
be selected in each of the four regions, collaboration will be sought from
the Universities of Chittagong, Mymensingh and Rajshahi in the matters re-
lating to recruitment of interviewers and supervision of their field work,
and editing and coding of data in the regions; the project staff will look
after the work in these four regions. The interviewers and supervisors will
be appointed on an ad-hoc basis and trained in the canvassing of the schedule,
in Dacca for a period of two weeks. The interviewers will edit the question-
naires before leaving the field. They will also code the data in the uni-
versity in the region. The punching, verification and processing of the data
will be done by the regular staff of the ISRT on an overtime basis, utilizing
its equipment. The project provides for two research assistants to assist in
the analysis. The report will be prepared by the Project Director and Deputy
Director.
5.        Coverage:  The survey covers a sample of eligible couples in four
concentrated thanas which were selected in the four regions of the country
for conducting the eight pilot schemes.
6.        Staff and Other Requirements:  The project provides the following
additions:
(a) Personnel: (i) One Project Director to plan and
execute the survey, analyze the data, and write
the report. (ii) Four research assistants to help
in field supervision and analysis of data. (iv) Two
stenographers to work for the Director and Deputy
Director. (v) One peon for the office. (vi) Twenty
interviewers (one male and four females in each
thana) to canvass questionnaires, edit and code
the data. (vii) Four supervisors (one in each
thana) to organize and supervise field work and
coding of data.



A   X 16
?age 3
(b)  Operating Costs:  (i) 12,000 punch cards. (ii) Hionorarium
to ISRT staff for punching and tabulation of data. (iii)
Honorarium to three staff members of the three regional
universities for collaborating on the project in the
recruitment of interviewers, and supervision of field
work and coding (the project staff will look after the
fourth region). (iv) Travel of interviewers, supervisors,
project staff and Advisory Committee Members. (v) Printing
of questionnaires and instruction manuals. (vi) Publication
of the report. (vi) 5 per cent service charge to be paid
to the University of Dacca for making its resources avail-
able for the project.
7.        Expected Results:  The survey provides benchmarks useful in
the assessment of improvements in the KAP levels in the four thanas as a
result of the pilot schemes.
8.        Internal Evaluation:  The basic data collected in the survey
will be checked for internal consistency and cross-checked with the
couple registration data for reliability. Assessment of quality of
the data will also be made in the final analysis.
9.        Cost:  The total cost of the project will be US$26,000 for one
year. The details are given at the end of this annex.
10.       Work Schedule:
a.   Appointment of a Project Director, a Deputy
Director and Research Assistants                      March 1975

survey                                                April 1975

B. Follow-up Surveys
First Follow-up Survey
11.       The details of the follow-up surveys would be worked out by the
concerned agencies later. The following indicates the broad objectives:
a.   Objectives:  To determine, in comparison to the
bench-marks, the improvements brought about by the
schemes in KAP and fertility reduction; and to
assess the relative ability of the different exec-
uting ministries to coordinate their efforts. Further,
comment from the sample population on the desirability
of the schemes from the viewpoint of the clients' re-
quirements and administrative and technical problems
should be obtained.
b.   Sample:  A sample of at least 2,500 currently married
women and a sub-sample of at least 1,000 of their husbands
will be selected. Half the areas from which the females
and males are drawn will be in common with the base-line
survey and the remaining areas will be new. A probability
sample of males and females will be drawn from each area.
c.   Levels of Comparison:  Based on surveys and other data it
will be possible to make comparisons for:
Mi) the common areas between the follow-up and base-
line survey;
(ii) between the group of four concentrated thanas and
a group of similar thanas in the four districts; and
(iii) between the group of four thanas and all thanas in
the four districts.
d.   Agency and Cost:  The PPS should arrange for the survey
with the help of ISRT and possibly other research insti-
tutions. In addition to the support for the infrastructure
of the PPS, the additional funds required for the survey
is estimated to be US$20,000.



.anec  5
2.       (- o3ze Tl-o--up Survey:  This s1hould  be undersa.ran at a time
coinciding with. the termination of the pilot schemes.
a.   Objectives:  Same as for the mid-term appraisal wi.th
greater emphasis on determination ofE the direct effects
of the individual schemes, and their combinations; ef-
fects of diffusion process; and non-program effects.
b.   Sample:  Same sample size as for the previous survey
will be drawn from different areas so that 25 percent
of them will be from common areas for the first and
second surveys, 25 percent of the first but not the
second survey, and 50 percent from new areas. Within
each area selected, a probability sample of the
required number of wives and husbands will be
drawn.
c.   Levels of Comparisons:  This sample survey's findings
can be compared with those of the first and second
surveys.
d.   Agency and Cost:  The PPS will also arrange for
this survey like the previous survey for which
US$20,000 is provided.
II. Other Pilot Thanas
13.       The KAP type of surveys should be conducted in the 15 thanas
(excluding the concentrated thanas) - before the schemes start for providing
the base-line survey (or alternatively a retrospective survey after the
scheme is in operation), and the other after twenty-four months of operation
of the scheme. The survey should have questions that reveal the changes
in levels of fertility, attitude toward family size and knowledge and practice
of contraceptives. The following describes the sample objectives and com-
parison levels for the surveys for each of the two pilot schemes taken in
combination in the same thanas.
Women's Functional Literacy and Use of
Model Farmers and Cooperative Managers
a.   ObJectives:
(i) to determine the increase in the level of KAP
in the community;



h-\NX 16
Page 6
(ii) to investigate the important aspects of the
functioning of the two schemes, such as reasons
for persons of various categories dropping out
of the schemes, adequacy of training,
problems in implementation of the schemes,
requirements of the community and what modi-
fications in the scheme should be made; and
(iii) to determine the extent of practice of contracep-
tion among the persons specially trained in the
schemes.
b.   Sample:  A total sample of 4,000 couples for each survey
will be selected from the 15 thanas for the KAP part of
the survey and both the husbands and wives will be inter-
viewed independently. Of these, 2,000 couples will be
from the village where only the scheme of model farmers
and cooperative managers is operating, and 2,000 couples
from the remaining villages of the 15 thanas. For the
second and third parts of the survey, 100 persons
trained as village organizers, 300 female cooperative
members trained in the literacy program, 100 cooperative
managers and 300 model farmers will be selected from
villages having both schemes. The same number of the
four categories of persons will be selected also from
other villages having only one scheme.
c.   Levels of Comparison:  Based on the survey and other
data, it will be possible to make comparisons of
important findings on KAP, between the two groups
of villages having one scheme or both schemes,
between these groups of villages and areas with
different combinations of other pilot schemes, and
with other areas not having any pilot scheme at all.
Similarly for the other part of the survey, comparisons
of different functional aspects of the schemes when
they are operated concurrently vis-a-vis wlhen only
one scheme is implemented.
d.   Agency and Cost:  The PPD should undertake the survey
in collaboration with appropriate institutions. Esti-
mated cost of the surveys would be US$53,000.
15.       Agricultural Assistants and Mothers' Clubs
a.   Objectives:
(i) relating to the first scheme: to study the impact
of the scheme on KAP;



Pa   7
(i):`  relating to the second scheme:  to study the impact
of the scheme on KAP and important functional aspects,
such as, adequacy of training given to different cate-
gories of persons, reasons for dropping out of the
scheme of persons trained, problems of following
the vocations, reactions of persons directly in-
volved in the schemes and of the public to the
operations;
(iii) relating to both: to determine the extent of
practice of contraception by the persons trained
under the schemes.
b.   Sample:  For that part of the survey which aims at
studying the impact, a representative sample of 2,000
couples for each survey will be drawn from the 15 thanas
(excluding the four concentrated thanas) and other mem-
bers of the couples will be interviewed. For the other
part of the survey, 100 village social workers, 100 ex-
tension agents and 1,000 mothers who ever joined the
clubs will be selected.
16.       Agency and Cost:  The PPD will contract this survey out to an
appropriate agency; the estimated cost would be US$39,700.
Seminars for School Teachers and Family Welfare Workers Motivation Kit
17.       The PPD should arrange for the assessment of efficacy of primary
and secondary school teacher seminars by:
a.   measurement of change in their knowledge, attitude and
practice of family planning;
b.   follow-up of the impact of teachers in extending the
knowledge of population problems in the school and the
community;
c.   the effectiveness of motivation kits on the performance
of family welfare workers.
A sample of about 20 villages with the scheme and 20 village without the
scheme from each thana should be ta'ken at random for the studies.
18.       Agency:  The PPD should give funds to the Institute of Educational
Research for undertaking this study. The estimated cost is US$9,000.

the centers:
a.   Utilization of available manpower and adequacy

1,000 pill acceptors will be selected on the basis of client records of

other methods, the monthly reports of the centers will be used to esti-
mate couple years of protection. The cost of the project will be appro-
ximately US$25,100.
21.       Women's Vocational Training Program
The women's vocational training program should be assessed in
terms of knowledge, attitude and practice of family planning among the
women receiving training and the trainers, the skills and knowledge
received through the scheme and the views of trainees on the technical
and administrative aspects of the scheme. A sample of about 500 women
should be taken covering the trainees at the thana, union and village
levels. The PPD should give the contract to one of the universities.
The estimated cost is US$25,000.
22.       Schemes of the Ministry of Information and Broadcasting
a.   Objectives:  To determine the coverage of population by
each scheme, the impact of each scheme on the YKAP of married
persons, and public reactions to the schemes.
b.   Sample:  One rural and one urban sample each of 1,500
households will be drawn and all married persons in the
selected households will be interviewed. For drawing
the samples, the procedures are suggested in Annex 13
describing the program of the Ministry of Information
and Broadcasting.
